Anhui Provincial Government Revises Types of Disaster Relief Grain 77

Dingbu Disaster Relief Grain Collection Office Abolished

Wuhu Dispatch: Liu Zhenhua, Chairman of the Anhui Provincial Government, believes that the types of disaster relief grain collected in various places in the province originally included ten types, such as black and white sesame, peanuts, sunflower seeds, melon seeds, and dried daylily and broad beans. He repeatedly requested exemptions from collection. Later, he received instructions from Chairman Chiang of the Nanchang Headquarters that the collection of disaster relief grain should be limited to what can be directly used as daily food for the people, and that collection in lieu of price or distribution in lieu of price should not be allowed. Miscellaneous grains that cannot be used as daily food or have very low yields should also be removed and exempted from collection. A revised list of types of disaster relief grain to be collected must be submitted for approval. In addition to wheat flour and rapeseed, which have already been exempted from collection, the Anhui Provincial Government specifically proposed revised lists of types of disaster relief grain to be collected and types of disaster relief grain originally collected for discussion at the provincial government's regular meeting, which has now been approved in accordance with the amendment. Furthermore, the provincial government, based on a report from Wang Youqi, Director of the Dingbu Disaster Relief Grain Office, stated that since the establishment of the Dingbu Office, the Suxu River has been dry for a long time, resulting in poor harvest. The grain from the Mei and Zhu branch offices of the general office are all exported to Liyang via the Suxu River. The Jiangsu Construction Department is currently dredging the Suxu River, and all ships have stopped running. The harvests from Mei and Zhu are completely non-existent. The river is about forty to fifty li long and cannot be dredged in a short period of time. Even after completion, this year's yield will be low due to the long drought, and future harvests will also be meager. The Jiepai branch office is also experiencing soaring grain prices, and the county government has issued a notice prohibiting transportation, making the harvest even less reliable. Therefore, it has submitted a report to the provincial government requesting that the Dingbu Disaster Relief Grain Collection Office and the Mei, Zhu, and Jiepai branch offices be abolished to avoid wasting funds. As for the Guojia Du and Huajin inspection stations, although disaster relief grain can be collected, they can be assigned to the Wuhu office for nearby management. The provincial government, recognizing the benefits of these facts, has approved the abolition of the offices and stations, and ordered the Wuhu office to collect and transport the disaster relief grain stored in Dingbu. (29th)

Post-Disaster Work Being Handled in Southern Jiangxi 78

Guangdong First Army Returns to Defend and Dispatches Troops for Pacification

Delegations from All Walks of Life Enter Jiangxi to Express Sympathy

Guangzhou Dispatch: The Jiangxi bandits recently fled west, leaving behind ruined houses wherever they passed. Southern Jiangxi bore the brunt of the impact and suffered the greatest losses. The area is a scene of devastation, and the local vitality urgently needs to be restored. Recently, the Guangdong First Army has been returning to their defense posts in Xinfeng, Sannan, Nankang, and Dayu. On the one hand, they are recuperating, and on the other hand, they are actively planning local construction and recruiting refugees. Yu Hanmou, the Commander of the First Army, has telegraphed his assumption of the position of Pacification Commander of the Sixth District of Jiangxi Province and is starting pacification, and has also formulated pacification measures to be implemented in order. The steps are as follows: (1) Dispatches

troops to search and suppress the remaining bandits, and encourages local Communists to reform themselves; (2) Conducts edification work, vigorously refutes Communist heresies, and instills the Three Principles of the People; (3) Investigates the population of villages, towns, and households in each district, and organizes joint defense; (4) Recruits refugees back to their hometowns to restore rural areas; (5) Undertakes relief efforts to support people's production; (6) Builds roads and repairs power lines; (7) Prohibits opium and gambling, and encourages mining. Of the above items, the most important is to vigorously implement pacification so that refugees can return, live in peace and work, and then all industries can be revived. However, the eleven counties in southern Jiangxi are adjacent to various places in the east, with overlapping mountains, and there are still over a thousand remnants of Ye Jianying's communist forces north of Junmen and Anyuan. Local communists frequently cause disturbances, and it is necessary to thoroughly eliminate them. The military headquarters has now dispatched portions of the Second Division under Ye Zhao to defend Gupei, Da Xiaowo, Huangni Pai, Jiudu Shui, Nankang, and Xincheng, responsible for pacifying each of those locations. It has dispatched the Independent Fourth Division under Deng Longguang to search for remaining bandits in Junmen, Xunwu, Anyuan, Chongshi, and Banshi. The First Army Training Regiment under Xie Xizhen is maintaining security near Dayu, and the Garrison Regiment under Zhao Lian is eliminating scattered bandits near Yujiang. As for local construction matters, the Pacification Headquarters is handling them separately. Previously, all sectors of Guangdong Province initiated a mass rally to express sympathy to the generals and soldiers fighting the communist bandits in southern Jiangxi, who resisted the westward fleeing brigands and defended the borders. They dispatched sympathy delegations to various destinations to express sympathy and provide supplies. The northern sympathy delegation, after departing, split into two routes to enter southern Jiangxi: one went to Xinfeng to express sympathy to the Second Division, and the other went to Dayu to express sympathy to the units subordinate to the First Army. They then returned to Nanxiong to express sympathy to the First Division and returned to Shaozhou to express sympathy to the Independent Second Brigade. On the 18th of this month, they transferred from Shaozhou to Lechang to express sympathy to the Fourth Division under Zhang Da, and then returned to Shaozhou and Guangzhou. The sympathy delegation consists of more than ten people. In each location, they held flag-giving ceremonies at the military headquarters, division headquarters, and brigade headquarters, and presented sympathy items, such as towels and other supplies. The regimental headquarters was treated to wine and meat. (December 22nd)

New Life Movement of the New Life Movement Promotion General Association 79

Glimpses of the Daily Lives of All Employees

Nanchang Dispatch: The New Life Movement Promotion General Association is the central hub for promoting the New Life Movement. The association's staff particularly emphasize practicing the New Life Movement themselves, as a model for the general public. The details of the staff's daily lives are described as follows:

▲Morning Exercises All employees of the association currently practice calisthenics and deep breathing exercises on the open-air lawn at 8:00 a.m. every morning to strengthen their physique. The exercises last for about half an hour, after which they enter the office to work, feeling more energetic. The exercises are led by the tall and burly Mr. Yan Baohang as the instructor.

▲Bathing In addition to focusing on health, the association also strongly promotes physical cleanliness. It has a bathroom with two bathtubs. Male employees are required to bathe every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday, while female employees bathe every Tuesday, Thursday, and Saturday. Sundays are designated as bath days for the workers, who provide their own bathing supplies.

▲Singing Educators with any foresight value music education. The association's staff recently formed a singing club, practicing every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday from 1:00 p.m. to 2:00 p.m., led and instructed by Ms. Zhang Zhiyuan, who studied music in France and has a deep understanding of it. The club rejects all vulgar and lewd songs. The staff is currently practicing the Party song and the New Life Movement song to sing them correctly.

▲Social Gatherings Proper entertainment is essential to adjust a monotonous life during leisure time. The association has formed a social club that holds gatherings once every half month. Employees are allowed to bring close friends or family members, but must obtain the consent of the person in charge beforehand. This club has already held two gatherings, chosen on Saturday evenings. All the programs are very exciting. It is said that the third social gathering is scheduled to be held on New Year's Eve this year, and there will be even more exciting events. It is said that Mr. Huang Guangji of the association will participate with his foreign wife.

▲Reading Students focus on studying diligently during their school days, but they should also continue to study in their spare time during their service. Recognizing this, the association has a reading club, with three directors appointed by Secretary Yan: Director Zhang Zhiyuan, Clerk Ji Ningge, and Manager Song Yinshan. The club's rules have been drafted and passed by the meeting. They were signed and promulgated by Secretary Yan on the 25th, and are recorded below: (1) Name: New Life Movement Promotion General Association, Colleagues' Reading Club. (2) Purpose: The purpose of this club is to increase knowledge and study academics. (3) Organization: This club has three directors appointed by the secretary of the New Life Movement General Association, responsible for handling club affairs. (4) Reading Scope: The reading scope of this club is defined as follows: New Life Category, Party Doctrine Category, Art Category, Military Category, History and Geography Category, Political Economy Category, National Studies Category, and others. (5) Research Method: In order to develop colleagues' specialties and promote the interest in joint research, the following methods are adopted: 1. Individual Speech: The speaker is solicited or selected by the chairman at the previous meeting. The topic is chosen by the speaker. 2. Joint Discussion: The discussion questions are decided at the previous meeting and a rapporteur is designated to research the topic and reference books. (6) Meeting Time: Meetings are held every two weeks, every Friday evening at 7:30 p.m., with a time limit of one and a half hours each time. (7) Covenant: Colleagues of this club should strictly abide by the following articles: 1. Study faithfully, 2. Accept criticism, 3. Adhere to time, 4. Respect order. (8) These rules will be implemented after being passed by a meeting of the colleagues of the reading club.

Songjiang

Frequent Robberies in Caojing Township 80

Caojing Township in Punan belongs to the eighth district of this county. Located on the coast, it has always been a haunt for bandits and robbers. This year, the township's agricultural production suffered a poor harvest, and unscrupulous elements took the opportunity to rise up, resulting in robbery cases almost every day. This has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Unexpectedly, at about 12:00 a.m. on the 25th, the home of Zhang Wencai, a villager in the 25th Tu of Caojing, was again raided by more than a dozen bandits speaking a local dialect. They ransacked the house, looting twenty bales of cotton, two shi of rice, over ten hemp bags, over ten pieces of clothing, and a small boat, carrying the loot south and escaping. The next day, the robbed small boat was found in the Dahe Port of this Tu. The case was reported to the local police station, and a search for the robbers was launched.

The county government, upon receiving orders from the provincial government, issued measures to celebrate New Year's Day and launch a year-end cleaning campaign, ordering subordinates to comply. It is reported that in addition to cleaning themselves on the 31st, various agencies have decided that schools in the city will be responsible for sweeping the streets, with County Magistrate Jin and others as commanders. Outside the city, the youth amateur service corps organized by the business community will be responsible, with the director of the Public Security Bureau and the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce as commanders. It is decided that the cleaning will take place at 10:00 a.m. on the 31st.

Wuxi

Female Workers Demand Wages, Labor-Police Clash 82

After the Xingji Silk Factory outside the South Gate's Tieshu Bridge closed down, it owed its employees over 3,000 yuan in wages. For days, female workers petitioned to demand their wages. After mediation by the Public Security Bureau, 80% of the November wages were paid first. This situation was reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now reported that at around 3:00 p.m. yesterday, the factory paid 75% of the November wages, and the Public Security Bureau and the Third Branch Bureau dispatched over 30 police officers to the factory to maintain order. Unexpectedly, Hakka female workers suddenly stopped local female workers from receiving their wages, resulting in a clash. The local female workers fled to the Third Branch Bureau of the Public Security Bureau, and the Hakka female workers followed them in, resulting in another clash with the police officers of the bureau. The two police officers who were injured, Lin Shide of Mengang and Tang Baohua of the office, were attacked. The female workers Zhou, Wang, Chen, and others also suffered serious waist injuries. The situation was serious. The branch bureau telegraphed the county government and the General Public Security Bureau, and dispatched security teams and mobile patrol teams to suppress the situation. A hooligan named Lu Hongfu, who was echoing and causing trouble, was arrested on the spot and taken to the bureau for interrogation. At the same time, the female workers were informed to receive their wages and not to cause trouble. The distribution was completed at around 6:00 p.m. The injured police officers Lin Shide and Tang Baohua, and the injured female workers Zhou, Wang, Chen, and others were sent to the Puren Hospital for treatment.

Minister of Education Wang Shijie and President of National Central University Luo Jialun came to Wuxi from Nanjing the night before yesterday, admiring the scenic mountains and rivers and natural scenery of our city. They stayed at the Taihu Hotel in Meiyuan, preparing to visit Meiyuan and Yuantouzhu. However, they encountered heavy rain and were unable to travel freely. They are scheduled to return to Nanjing by car today.

Wine-Brewing Farmers Petition the County Bureau 84

Farmers in the southern Quan and Hua Dafang village areas of the third district of this county brew a small amount of wine in their spare time to prepare for self-drinking because they are near Taihu Lake and the water source is clear. This year, the Tobacco and Wine License Tax Office suddenly levied license taxes on wine-brewing farmers and arbitrarily arrested law-abiding citizens with armed police officers, resulting in disputes. Yesterday, Xu Shaoshan, Mo Yongsen, Zhang Songyun, and other representatives of wine-brewing farmers from these two towns led more than 100 villagers to petition the county government, demanding exemption from taxation. They also stated that wine-brewing households do not sell in stores and are different from taverns. The head of the second section, Fei Yunnong, came out to meet them and promised to send someone to investigate and verify the matter. They then went to the Public Security Bureau to petition, requesting the withdrawal of the eighth branch bureau and assisting police officers. Director Chen immediately dispatched Inspector Wang to meet them and instructed them that since they had filed a complaint with the provincial bureau, they should wait quietly for the province to handle the matter. The police officers assisting in the enforcement were allowed to withdraw. The representatives were satisfied and left.

County Magistrate Wu, recognizing that since the winter, theft cases have occurred frequently in the urban and rural areas, which is very concerning for local security. Changzhou

County Government Executes Bandit and Drug Trafficker 86

In the case of Chen Yugeng's home in Gaomei Township, Wu County, being robbed by the bandit Yang Heshang and his gang on June 19th, 1932, and Chen Yugeng being shot and killed, the township reported the case to the county government for apprehension. Yang Heshang fled without a trace and was not caught. The criminal recently returned to Qianheng Town, believing that enough time had passed, and privately trafficked in drug pills for a living. Huang Yuncheng, a patrol officer from the seventh branch station of the Yun Cunzhen Public Security Station, captured a drug pill addict who stated that all the drug pills were bought from Yang Heshang's home. Yang Heshang was immediately arrested, taken to the county for interrogation. After several interrogations, the criminal confessed to trafficking drugs and robbery and murdering Chen Yugeng. He was sentenced to death. The provincial government approved the execution by telegram on the 29th. County Magistrate Hou dispatched a police officer to bring the criminal Yang Heshang to the court at around 2:00 p.m., verified his identity, and sent him bound to the Fengweidun execution ground for execution.

Due to the county-run eight elementary schools being owed seven months of teachers' salaries, making it impossible to maintain a livelihood, a joint petition was made to the Education Bureau. Upon hearing this, the school representatives felt it was a drop in the bucket and would not solve the problem. Another temporary meeting was convened, and as a result of discussions, the representatives all expressed their intention to strike in order to urge the authorities to pay attention. Therefore, yesterday (the 27th) afternoon, a unanimous strike began, awaiting a resolution.

Bandit Activity Resurges in the Fifth District 92

In the fifth district of this county, during the autumn of this year, a large number of bandit gangs were entrenched in various places, including Da Lizhuang, Zhou Jinxiang, and Tangjiabao, engaging in widespread kidnapping and robbery. Nine out of ten households in the villages were robbed clean. Later, after Regiment Commander Yang of the Provincial Security Team's Third Regiment led troops to suppress them, the bandits fled into the jurisdiction of Baoying County, a neighboring county, specifically to Da Xiaoguanzhuang, Wadian, Bai Duo, and Pan Shakou in the fifth district. They continued to kidnap and rob in various places. Recently, after the county's military and police inflicted a severe blow, the bandits, realizing that they could not establish a foothold, fled in droves back to Zhou Jinxiang and other places in the fifth district of this county, plotting to operate. Therefore, the villagers are extremely frightened, fearing further devastation by the bandits.

Hangzhou

Elderly Man Commits Suicide Due to Debt 95

Wang Aqi, the owner of a glutinous rice dumpling shop at No. 231 Qingtai Road in Hangzhou City, is 63 years old and has two sons. The eldest son is doing business outside, and the second son assists with the shop at home. Recently, due to poor business, he has accumulated debts of over 1,600 yuan. Creditors were pressing him hard for repayment. Wang Aqi was driven to desperation and developed a pessimistic view of life. Yesterday morning, he hanged himself in his room. His son discovered him, but it was too late to save him. The responsible Public Security Bureau telegraphed the court to send personnel to examine the body and prepare it for burial.

Pregnant Woman Crushed to Death at Soup Kitchen 96

Since its opening, the Hangzhou soup kitchens have been extremely crowded with commoners seeking food. The Seventh Soup Kitchen at Baize Temple outside Gengshan Gate has an especially large number of people receiving soup. Zhou, a farmer from Wulong Temple, and a Mrs. Lin were both heavily pregnant. For the sake of survival, they still went to the factory to receive soup every day. Yesterday, while receiving soup, Mrs. Lin was pushed too hard and collapsed on the spot, giving birth. People carried her home, but both the mother and child died on the way. Soon after, Mrs. Zhou also gave birth to her child. Neighbors of the soup kitchen, fearing a repeat occurrence, built a thatched shed in front of the soup distribution area to provide a place for rest and recuperation.

The county magistrate, upon receiving the order, knew that his crime was unforgivable and is now seeking people to smooth things over with Le Jialiang's family in hopes of avoiding prosecution.

Northeast Postal Communication Issue Resolved 100

Receiving and Forwarding Mail Starts on January 10th

Parcel and Remittance Services Start on February 1st

Since the suspension of postal services in the four northeastern provinces, communication between people inside and outside the customs has been greatly inconvenient. According to a conversation with a responsible official of the Postal Administration, the three business areas of various types of mail, parcels, and remittances to and from that province will be transferred through a transfer agency at Shanhaiguan and Gubeikou, entering the customs on January 10th and February 1st. Mail will also use special stamps, and if other invalid stamps are mistakenly affixed, the transfer agency will be responsible for paying the deficiency and will not collect the deficiency from the recipient. The original text of the post office notice is transcribed below as an announcement: In order to facilitate the public, the three businesses of mail, parcels, and remittances will be handled by the two transfer agencies at Shanhaiguan and Gubeikou. All mail destined for Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Rehe, and the four provinces, if the province and place names are clearly written on the envelope and there are no false organization words, will be accepted and forwarded starting on January 10th. Parcels and remittances will be handled according to regulations starting on February 1st. This is hereby announced.

Foreign Exchange Rose to Six Jiao Yesterday 104

But This Is Common During the Settlement Period

The foreign exchange rate opened at six jiao at 8:00 a.m. and 12:00 p.m. yesterday in the money market, an increase of five fen compared to yesterday. Reporters from the New Voice News learned yesterday from the money industry that the national currency exchange rate is divided into two markets, morning and afternoon, each day, and the corresponding market price is determined according to the urgency of supply and demand in the market. Although it has risen to six jiao now, this is a common occurrence during each settlement period. For example, in the years 1917, 1918, 1919, 1921, 1922, 1923, 1924, and 1932, the silver exchange rate rose to a peak of seven qian at that time.

Prelude to National Goods Entering the South Seas 105

Song Faxiang Wrote to the National Chamber of Commerce Federation

Soliciting National Goods to Be Shipped to the South Seas for Display

Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Chamber of Commerce Federation of the Republic of China, received a letter from Song Faxiang, Consul-General stationed in Batavia, yesterday, stating: "Chairman Kanghou, I have returned to China on leave to attend the Fifth National Congress and investigate the status of national goods in order to promote Sino-Dutch trade. It was a great pleasure to meet with you and discuss the issue of national goods entering the South Seas. I am also very grateful for your kind hospitality. I apologize for not being able to visit each of you before my departure due to time constraints. I have arrived at my post on the morning of the 11th of this month and am preparing to report the findings of this trip to the overseas Chinese community here and discuss ways to promote national goods. I have received your letter of November 24th, in which you express your great concern for the promotion of national goods. I am deeply gratified and have instructed the Dutch East Indies Chamber of Commerce Federation to inform its members to join your association as members in order to facilitate communication. I will send another letter once I have a reply. Regarding the promotion of national goods, I intend to start by setting up a national goods exhibition hall so that the overseas Chinese businessmen here can have a good understanding of national goods and thus make it easier to promote them. I would like to ask your association to find ways to solicit various national goods samples, list prices, and have them shipped to the Dutch East Indies Chamber of Commerce Federation or this Consulate for display by the Java Shipping Company. I would appreciate your advice on how to proceed. I hereby inform you and express my gratitude. With best wishes. Song also enclosed 11 official letters, asking the National Chamber of Commerce Federation to forward them to the China National Goods Maintenance Association, the China National Products Manufacturers Association, and 11 other organizations respectively, to express thanks."

New Life Movement Promotion Conference Resolved to Implement Measures 106

To Proceed in Eight Areas

The Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Conference, in order to actively implement the New Life Movement, specifically resolved various implementation measures at the fourth meeting of the executive committee, divided into eight areas:

Prohibition of Radio Broadcasting 107

"Regulations on the Prohibition of Wireless Radio Broadcasting": (1) Wireless radio broadcasting stations must register with the Education and Social Bureaus before they can begin operations. (2) The daily broadcast programs and advertisements must be submitted to the Education Bureau for review and approval three days in advance before they can be broadcast. (3) Wireless radio broadcasting stations must not broadcast lyrics or advertisements that are detrimental to public morals, promote superstition, or are deceptive in nature. (4) Wireless radio broadcasting stations should broadcast the following materials as much as possible: 1. Propaganda of Kuomintang principles, 2. Propaganda of the New Life Movement, 3. Lectures on intellectual and moral education, 4. Accurate news of current events, 5. Lyrics that awaken the national spirit, 6. Words and ideas that are beneficial to the world and people's hearts. (5) Those who do not comply with these regulations or repeatedly refuse to mend their ways may be punished jointly by the Public Security Bureau and the Education Bureau at their discretion. (6) These regulations shall be implemented by the Municipal Government after being reviewed and approved by the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Conference.

Rectification of City Appearance 108

"Measures for Rectifying the City Appearance": (1) (A) In terms of walking: (1) Pedestrians and vehicles on the road must keep to the left. (2) Pedestrians' clothing and hats must be neat and clean. (3) Pedestrians on the road must not smoke or eat food. (4) Men and women walking together must not engage in inappropriate behavior. (5) Prohibit bizarre clothing and grotesque appearances. (6) Prohibit loud noises, shouting, and gathering to quarrel. (B) In terms of streets and markets: (1) Post advertisements in designated places. (2) Sweep and water the roads and alleys at all times. (3) Notify residents not to dry clothes along the street. (4) Advise citizens not to urinate or defecate in public places. (5) Pay attention to ditches to prevent the accumulation of sewage. (6) No street stalls may be set up along important streets. (7) Send beggars to institutions for education and care. (8) Prohibit vendors from shouting and selling in strange voices. (9) Prohibit feudal escorts and religious festivals.

Civil Servants 109

"Measures for Government Employees to Practice the New Life Movement": (A) In terms of facilities: (1) Clean and tidy up the houses every day. (2) Store documents and equipment in designated places. (3) Furnishings should be simple and unadorned. (4) All kinds of equipment must be purchased from domestic goods. (5) Public sanitation facilities must be thorough. (6) Strictly prevent the misuse and waste of public goods and stationery. (7) Clerical and accounting must be honest and clear. (8) Set up New Life slogans in prominent places. (9) Erect flagpoles and raise and lower the flags every morning and evening. (10) Clearly mark the entrances of various places. (B) In terms of personnel: (1) Base the advancement and retreat of staff on morality and ability. (2) Officials should set an example to guide others. (3) Strictly observe office hours and pay attention to attendance. (4) Posture when sitting, standing, and walking must be correct. (5) No smoking, drinking, gambling, or prostitution. (6) No idle talk or play during office hours. (7) Treat people with kindness and sincerity. (8) Read useful books in your spare time. (9) Be loyal to your duties and everyone should be responsible. (8) In terms of public service: (1) Get up early every day, wash, and dress neatly. (2) Do your job conscientiously every day. (3) Treat people with kindness and sincerity. (4) No smoking, gambling, prostitution, or drinking. (5) Be faithful and diligent in doing what you are told. (6) Pay attention to the practical protection of all public property. (7) Do not linger outside when on duty. (8) Do not interrupt or talk too much unless asked. (9) Be especially well-behaved and clean when on duty.

Restaurants and Hotels 110

"Measures for Restaurants and Hotels to Practice the New Life Movement": (1) Clean all tables and chairs thoroughly. (2) Do not leave dust or dirt on windows, doors, or corners. (3) Make sure the kitchen chimney is unobstructed. (4) Cooks and waiters must be dressed neatly. (5) Bowls, chopsticks, and other utensils must be placed in designated places. (6) Utensils and dishes must be purchased from domestic goods. (7) Cooking must be very clean. (8) Do not put indecent paintings or calligraphy on the walls of the house. (9) Clean tableware and towels with boiling water. (10) Strictly prevent flies and gnats from contaminating raw and cooked food. (11) Do not mix and sell rotten or stale food. (12) Food prices must be clearly marked. (13) Waiters must be dignified and courteous. (14) Arrive late every night and must close by midnight. (15) Do not print gambling tickets or solicit prostitutes for customers.

Inns and Bathhouses 111

"Measures for Inns to Practice the New Life Movement": (1) Clean the inn every day. (2) Uniform and number the tea attendants and servants. (3) Wash bedclothes and bedding immediately after use. (4) Kill mosquitoes, flies, lice, and rats. (5) Do not allow guests to make loud noises. (6) Strictly prohibit gambling, prostitution, and smoking opium. (7) Interrogate guests with suspicious behavior. (8) Clearly mark room prices separately. (9) Attendants must not demand tips from guests. (10) Cooked meals must be cooked cleanly. (11) Boil towels and utensils in boiling water after use. (12) Report any major incidents involving guests to the police station immediately. (13) Do not conceal items lost by guests. (14) Send guests with sudden illnesses to the hospital quickly. (15) Clean and disinfect toilets and toilet utensils daily. (16) Provide appropriate books and newspapers for guests to pass the time. "Measures for Bathhouses to Practice the New Life Movement": (1) Clean the bathhouse every day. (2) Make sure the indoor temperature is suitable. (3) Wash towels in boiling water after use. (4) Boil bathrobes and teaware in boiling water after use. (5) Clearly mark towels for washing face and body separately. (6) Do not allow guests with infectious diseases to mix in. (7) Do not allow shop assistants to be shirtless and naked. (8) Do not demand tips from customers. (9) Provide more medicines and fewer cosmetics and fragrances. (10) Provide appropriate books and newspapers for guests to pass the time. "Measures for Barber Shops to Practice the New Life Movement": (1) Clean the shop every day. (2) Wash towels and cloths in boiling water after use. (3) Sharpen knives and scissors and keep them clean. (4) Check electrical appliances once a day. (5) Sweep up hair and fruit peels at any time. (6) Uniform and number the shop assistants. (7) Charge according to the fixed price and do not overcharge. (8) Do not allow dirty or shirtless customers. (9) Provide appropriate books and newspapers for guests to pass the time. (10) Provide more medicines and fewer cosmetics and fragrances.

Entertainment Venues 112

"Measures for Entertainment Venues to Practice the New Life Movement": (1) Clean entertainment venues at any time. (2) Provide all kinds of sanitation facilities. (3) Clearly write and hang up the various seat prices. (4) Do not deduct ticket rebates arbitrarily. (5) Do not allow performances to be detrimental to public morals. (6) Uniform and number employees. (7) Leave some lights on when showing movies. (8) Open according to regulations and do not open all night. (9) Do not use improper advertisements to attract tourists. (10) Check props before performances. (11) Discourage viewers from clapping, cheering, and making noise.

Train Stations and Docks 113

"Measures for Public Buses and Electric Trains to Practice the New Life Movement": (1) Clean the inside and outside of the carriages every day. (2) Dress neatly when driving and selling tickets. (3) Do not place large items on the car. (4) Neither party should cheat when selling tickets. (5) Do not open the doors until the car has stopped. (6) No smoking, eating, or shouting in the car. (7) Do not allow passengers on the car when the carriage is full. (8) Strictly prohibit talking to customers while driving. "Measures for Train Stations and Docks to Practice the New Life Movement": (1) Clean the seats, doors, and windows everywhere. (2) Post road signs as needed. (3) Uniform and number porters and runners. (4) No smoking, eating, or shouting in the station. (5) Porters and runners should charge according to regulations when carrying goods for passengers. (6) Strictly prohibit porters and runners from unreasonably soliciting or demanding things. (7) Do not allow vendors to mix and sell unclean food. (8) Strictly observe order when boarding and alighting from vehicles. (9) Do not allow large luggage to enter or exit through windows. (10) Make sure the lights are bright at night. (11) Sell tickets and exchange for fair rebates. (12) Attendants should answer passengers' questions in detail and courteously. (13) Provide clocks and spittoons for guests to use.

Hankou Chamber of Commerce Writes to Shanghai Chamber of Commerce That Legal Silver Currencies Are Universally Valid 114

No More Price Differences or Rebates Allowed

To Be Implemented Starting Tomorrow on New Year's Day

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce received a letter from the Hankou Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "The Hankou Bankers Association and the Money Trade Association jointly issued a letter stating: 'Since the abolition of taels and the introduction of yuan, the demand for hard currency has increased. The types of hard currency in our country were originally very complex, and the weight and fineness were inconsistent. Often, coins minted in Province A cannot circulate in Province B, and this is even considered a precedent. In Hankou, only a few types of silver coins, such as those with the image of Sun Yat-sen, the images of Presidents Yuan and Xu, those made in Hubei Province, and those of the Great Qing Dynasty, have been commonly used in recent years. Other silver dollars minted in various provinces cannot be circulated arbitrarily. This situation should be restricted if the coins do not meet the legal fineness and weight. However, it is not right to reject them all indiscriminately. It is necessary to promote the unification of the monetary system. The two associations held a joint meeting on December 4th and decided to follow suit and implement it from January 1st of the 24th year. We will send separate letters to the Provincial Chambers of Commerce and ask them to inform their members.

80,000 Bags of Foreign Rice Arrived Yesterday 115

The Last Batch of the Year

The last batch of 80,000 bags of Saigon rice, ordered by various rice merchants in this city from foreign firms such as British firm Dafu Tailong Heyi, arrived in Shanghai yesterday on two Norwegian ships. After import, they were sent to the Zhonghua Wharf opposite Xuejia Wharf to unload, preparing to be sold after the market opens next year. Because new goods of various gangs, guest glutinous rice, and foreign rice have been transported to Shanghai, and the inventory is crowded, the market price has fallen by two or three cents every day. According to observations in the rice industry market, there is hope for a rebound after the market opens in the new spring.

Spanish Training Ship Arrives in Shanghai for a Visit 119

According to the Zi Lin Bao, the Spanish training ship Elcano, carrying 230 sailors, 38 naval cadets, and 17 officers, commanded by Captain Fernan, arrived in Shanghai on Friday (the 28th). It is scheduled to depart for Yokohama and Honolulu at dawn on Thursday (January 3rd), planning to return to its home country via the United States, with a voyage abroad lasting approximately ten months. Among the junior officers are several recent graduates from the ship. Members of the press who boarded the ship for a visit were guided by a special commissioner. The ship has four masts, a tonnage of several thousand tons, and is equipped with auxiliary engines that are only used when the wind is weak. The Spanish community in Shanghai has been busy welcoming the ship's crew. It is noted that in 1927, a group of Spanish naval cadets also visited Shanghai.

Chinese Young Aviator Cao Shiong Wins Honors in French Aviation Competitions, Winning Numerous Championships, to Participate in Long-Distance Race from France to Vietnam Next Month 124

Shanghai News Agency reports that after Sun Tonggang, another young Chinese aviator, Cao Shiong, from Yiyang, Hunan, only twenty-two years old, went abroad in the nineteenth year of the Republic and has been studying in France for five years. He is proficient in technology and has won numerous aviation championships. Newspapers in Paris, Hong Kong, and other places have repeatedly reported on his achievements. Yesterday, Mr. Nie Haifan of the Municipal Education Bureau, a friend of Mr. Cao, informed reporters of the details as follows.

Diligent Study, Highly Regarded 125

When Mr. Cao went abroad, he applied to the Ministry of Education for Self-Funded Study in France Certificate No. 767. After arriving in France, he immediately enrolled in the aviation school of the Paris Aviation Association. In April of the twentieth year of the Republic, he was admitted to the Lyon French Aviation Department's Aviation Specialty School to study civil aviation. He graduated in August of the twenty-second year of the Republic with excellent grades and was allowed to continue his research in the military aviation department. He is currently studying mechanics and has been honored by the Rhône Southeast Aviation Association and invited to become a qualified member. Mr. Cao is the first Chinese to join the association.

Numerous Competitions, Multiple Championships 126

In June of this year, Mr. Cao participated in the long-distance race of the French Southeast Aviation Association's flying team. He flew his "One-Two-Five" aircraft from Lyon, traversing dense fog as if it were a clear sky, passing through fifteen large and small cities over six days. He remained energetic and showed no signs of fatigue. His performance was the best in the entire team, and he was welcomed and donated to by various French circles. He also accompanied the French Minister of Finance, Mr. Tardieu, and led his entire family to participate in local award ceremonies and exhibitions, where he was highly praised and regarded as a leading young Chinese aviator. In October of this year, he participated in the second international aviation competition, departing from France and arriving in Arlan City in Algiers, Africa, with excellent results. The local governor led a team to welcome him and extended warm hospitality. The voyage covered more than 5,000 miles, and Mr. Cao won first place in the team again. On October 25th, he flew from Arlan City to Egypt and other places.

Participating in a Long-Distance Race Next Month 127

In January of next year, he will participate in a long-distance race from France to Annam. It is hoped that Mr. Cao will win glory for our country and win the championship. Mr. Cao's expenses for studying abroad have reached more than 50,000 yuan. In addition to a subsidy of 3,000 yuan from the Hunan Provincial Government, he has been self-supporting. Recently, due to the high cost of living in France and the high expenses of aviation training, it is difficult to support himself. It is hoped that the government will provide assistance to this talented individual who can benefit the world, so that he can achieve great things.

Updates on the Emergency Relief Efforts 128

The Emergency Relief Donation Association has been working diligently day and night for a month since its establishment, and is still working as usual even on Sundays. Because the schools are on vacation, only Zhuangjing Primary School has submitted donations and receipt stubs, totaling one yuan in silver dollars and thirty-five cents in small silver coins. The worker's general donations are entrusted to the Shanghai Bank for collection, but they are also temporarily suspended for one day due to the bank's holiday.

The Emergency Relief Donation Association previously sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce regarding the general donations from various trade associations in the business community, requesting the Chamber of Commerce to handle the matter. The Chamber of Commerce specifically instructed various trade associations to raise funds quickly. Recently, various trade associations have submitted the completed donations to the Emergency Relief Donation Association in large numbers. Furthermore, the Fire Engine Cotton Industry Association sent a letter to the Association, claiming to be philanthropists who are always concerned about disaster relief, but will follow the instructions of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce in all actions, regarding the Association as a mixed organization, and requesting that the Association not solicit general donations in the future. After receiving the letter, the Emergency Relief Donation Association believed that the Association's wording was inappropriate and explained that the Association was formed by Party, government, and military organs and various organizations throughout the city to be responsible for raising funds for emergency relief in disaster areas. Why is it being called a mixed organization? Furthermore, the general donations from various trade associations have already been notified by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce for compliance, but the Association has not implemented them and still claims to follow the instructions of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce in all actions, which is contradictory. This year's disasters in various places are severe, and all citizens should reduce their spending and enthusiastically donate to help those in need. It is hoped that the Association will adhere to the principle that saving people in disasters is saving people and saving people is saving themselves, and make efforts to solicit donations.

Since the commencement of the household donation campaign, it has been greatly supported by the residents who enthusiastically donate, and the results have been good. Although it was raining heavily yesterday, personnel were still dispatched to carry publicity materials and promote and solicit donations from house to house.

Representatives from Langxi County, Southern Anhui, Arrive in Shanghai to Beg for Relief 129

Langxi County in southern Anhui has been suffering from drought for years, and bandits are rampant. Furthermore, this year's autumn harvest only yielded more than 200,000 piculs, leaving approximately 120,000 people without food. In all four directions, people are eating wild vegetables and sweet potato vines every day, and they are now running out. People are abandoning their children on the streets and sitting and waiting to die, which is heartbreaking. In addition, the Anhui government is pressing for grain very urgently, and the people cannot bear it. Therefore, representatives Zhang Shanzi, Wu Liutang, Xie Yutian, and Wang Zongde were publicly elected to appeal to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Relief Committee in the capital. They have been granted permission by the Anhui Province to reduce financial levies and have gone to Shanghai to visit the Drought Relief Committee, earnestly requesting that relief be released early to save the disaster-stricken people.

Jardine Matheson's New Pinghe Steamer to Sail the Shanghai-Hankou Route 135

Passenger Seats Completely Renewed

Sailing on January 5th

The British-owned Jardine Matheson's Pinghe steamer originally sailed the Shanghai-Yichang route. This year, the company sold the older Lianhe steamer to the Sanbei Company for 185,000 yuan, renaming it Mingxing. It is currently under repair in the factory. However, in order to replenish the Yangtze River steamer, Jardine Matheson specifically transferred the Yichang steamer Pinghe to the Shanghai-Hankou route. Before being reassigned, the ship was overhauled at the local Rui Rong factory, adding a large number of passenger seats and adding first, second, and third class cabins. The interior decoration of the ship has been completely renovated, making it magnificent and outstandingly beautiful. At the same time, the service and reception have been improved, and special attention has been paid to the food for the passengers. Currently, all the work has been completed, and the company is approved to officially dispatch it to the Yangtze River route on January 5th. In the future, it will sail every Wednesday and Saturday, and the ship's name will be changed to New Pinghe.

Can Arrive in Osaka Tonight

The Beitai steamer of the Northern Shipping Company, located at 29 Gongguan Road in the French Concession, with a tonnage of 2,400 tons, was chartered by a Japanese company this spring from the Tianjin head office to sail to Japan, Taiwan, Korea, and other places. It is not yet known whether the ship was damaged after running aground. The original telegram is recorded as follows: Hua (that is, the company's Beihua steamer) received a telegram from Tai (that is, the Beitai steamer) stating: "Got out of danger at 2:00 PM (on the 29th), expected to arrive in Osaka tonight."

Peide Necktie Company Announced Liquidation Yesterday 138

Possible to Resume Business

The Peide Necktie Company, located at 355 Sichuan Road, has been open for many years and has a manufacturing plant at 7 Fuxiang Lane, Tiantong Road, Zhabei. Its business has been good. Last year, it expanded its scope and added a Western-style clothing department. It was still able to maintain initially, but recently, due to the sluggish market and high expenses, its business gradually declined and became unsustainable. Therefore, it was forced to announce liquidation yesterday and engaged Attorney Zhan Jifeng to represent the company in notifying the liquidation. It is understood that the company's debts are approximately 100,000 yuan, but it can offset what others owe it, so there is still a possibility of resuming business.

Ports Frozen in Yingkou, Andong, etc., Ships Suspended 139

Goods Shipped by Train Instead

Scheduled to Open for Navigation in the Spring

Shipping companies operating in Yingkou, Andong, and other places, such as Zhengji, Zhaoxing, Northern, Zhendong, Yuda, Haichang, Datongxing, etc., have suspended operations due to the freezing and closure of the ports. All ships have been rerouted to Tianjin, Weihaiwei, Yantai, Longkou, Qinhuangdao, Dalian, and other ports, mainly to load goods. Goods from the Northeast are now shipped by train to Dalian, and then loaded onto ships to be transported south. It is expected that the ports will open for navigation by the end of March next year.

Fire at Sanxin Silk Weaving Factory 143

The Sanxin Silk Weaving Factory, located at 2 Yuqing Lane, Luban Road, Xieshi Road, Nanshi, caught fire at around 2:00 AM last night. The motor suddenly short-circuited while the factory was operating, burning the factory building. All the workers rushed to put out the fire, but because it was difficult to get water and the raw materials on the machines were mostly flammable, the fire blazed fiercely and broke through the roof for a time. The firefighters from the Second District Fire Brigade arrived after hearing the news and quickly extinguished the fire. All the property and goods in the factory were reduced to ashes, with losses estimated at several thousand yuan. However, the neighboring houses were not affected, and all the workers escaped from the fire without injury.

Zhou Asan and Others Sentenced for Trafficking Red Pills 144

Detective Xu Shunlin of the Hongkou Police Station, at around 9:00 PM the night before last, cracked a ring selling the drug "red pills" at 335 Xi'an Road, arresting the ringleader Zhou Are from Funing, along with customers Wang Are, Lu Baochang, suspects Zhu Yurong, Fan Yongsheng, and others, and bringing them, along with the red pills and smoking paraphernalia, to the police station. The next morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Attorney Li Zhishan of the Public Works Bureau presented the previous circumstances and requested an investigation. Next, Detective Xu reported the details of the case. Judge Xiao Xie Fen interrogated the defendants clearly and sentenced Zhou Are to one year and six months of imprisonment, Wang Are to thirty days of detention, and Lu Baochang to a fine of thirty yuan. Zhu Yurong and Fan Yongsheng were acquitted and released, and the evidence was confiscated.

Abduction and Sale of a Girl Leads to Sentencing 145

Bao Jiuru Sentenced to Two Years of Imprisonment

On the 14th of this month at 3:35 PM, Lan Ying, the four-year-old daughter of Lu Shi, a woman from Tongzhou residing at 605 Huasheng Road, was lured away from her doorstep by a criminal without a trace. The case was reported to the Yulin Road police station, which dispatched detectives Li Pengfei and Wu Shoushan. They apprehended four suspects, including Bao Jiuru (a relative of the victim's mother), Miao Yulin from Changzhou, Wang Fuyuan, and Zhang Asi from Jiangbei, at various locations such as 175 Yangzhou Road and the Tianbao Road Bridge in Zhabei. Interrogation revealed that Lu's daughter, Lan Ying, had been sold to Huo Su, a Cantonese woman residing at 47 Dengtuo Road, for 38 yuan, which was then divided among them. The detectives went to Huo Su's residence to search for Lu's daughter, but were unsuccessful. Huo Su claimed that she had been temporarily placed in the care of Liang Su, a fellow villager residing at 320 Gong'an Li, Wusong Road. The detectives secretly went to the address and rescued Lu's daughter, bringing her and Huo Su back to the police station. They were handed over to the First Special District Court. Huo Su was released on a 300-yuan surety, while the others were remanded in custody. The girl was returned to her mother, Lu Shi. This was previously reported in this newspaper. The day before yesterday, Judge Xiao Xieffen continued the trial in the Third Criminal Court. Huo Su did not appear, but her lawyer claimed that she was unaware of the court date and requested leniency. Judge Xiao, after thoroughly examining the defendants, sentenced Bao Jiuru to two years of imprisonment and Miao Yulin, Wang Fuyuan, and Zhang Asi to eight months each. The number of days spent in detention prior to the final judgment will be counted at a rate of two days of detention for one day of imprisonment. Su's case will be heard at a later date.

Sun Guanyuan Sentenced for Smoking Opium Substitute 146

Other Charges Dropped

Wang Guangqi, a Chinese detective at the Hongkou Police Station, learned that Sun Guanyuan from Pudong, residing in room 19 of the Xi'an Hotel at 98 Xi'an Road, was manufacturing materials for red pills, a type of drug, for profit. He sent an informant with 140 yuan in marked bills to arrange a purchase, scheduled for 3:00 PM on the 21st of this month. At the appointed time, the informant accompanied Chinese and foreign detectives to arrest Sun. They found him lying in bed, eating red pills under a lamp, with 36 pills beside him. They also discovered a large package of medicinal materials, weighing over 40 pounds, and several dozen yuan of the marked money under the bed, along with a set of opium smoking paraphernalia. They were handed over to the First Special District Court. The day before yesterday, Judge Xiao Xieffen continued the trial. (Note: The medicinal materials were purchased from the Sino-European Pharmacy on Guangdong Road.) Li Zhishan, a lawyer for the Public Works Department, stated that the medicinal materials had been tested by a doctor and found to contain no morphine, and requested that they, along with the money, be returned. The defendant insisted that the medicinal materials were not for making red pills, contained no toxic substances, and were bought by Chen Bingkun, who was currently at large, in an attempt to frame him. Judge Xiao sentenced Sun Guanyuan to four months of imprisonment for smoking an opium substitute, acquitted him of the other charges, confiscated the opium smoking paraphernalia and red pills, and ordered the money and medicinal materials to be returned to the Chinese detective who handled the case.

Shanghai-Taicang Bus Company Issues Discount Tickets 149

Rules for Free Rides Established

To facilitate travel for passengers, the Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Company will issue a new type of discount ticket starting January 1, 1935. The tickets are available in denominations of ten, twenty, and thirty trips. A ten-trip ticket contains ten single-trip tickets, which can be used until they are exhausted, and so on for the other denominations. The price of a ten-trip ticket is 80% of the original fare, and it is valid for 40 days. The price of a twenty-trip ticket is 75% of the original fare, and it is valid for 80 days. The price of a thirty-trip ticket is 70% of the original fare, and it is valid for 126 days. All tickets require a 2.5-inch photograph. Those wishing to purchase tickets must provide their name, destination, and the type of ticket they wish to purchase and contact each station. In addition, the company has established the following rules for free and half-price tickets starting January 1, 1935: (1) Special Ride Pass: Each organization is limited to one leader who can enjoy preferential treatment by obtaining a special ride pass, which must include a photograph of the holder. (2) Military and Police Special Ride Pass: Used in the same way as a monthly pass, but without a photograph, and is specifically for use by military and police organizations. Users must wear a uniform and insignia. If they are investigating a case and it is inconvenient to wear a uniform, but they wear the insignia or badge, leniency may be considered. (3) Military and Police Temporary Free Ride Pass: Although this pass is labeled "Military and Police," it is actually only for the security team stationed from Liuhe to Shanghai and the provincial security teams in Baoshan, Yanghang, Liuhang, Luodian, Dachang, and during the winter defense period. It is issued temporarily by the commanding officer with a letter of proof that the ride is for official business. Users must wear a uniform and insignia. Those who only wear a uniform without insignia or only wear insignia without a uniform may not use the pass. (4) Half-Price Ride Pass: The pass must have a photograph attached. With the pass, a half-price ticket can be purchased at the ticket office. A temporary blue carbon copy is filled out in duplicate with the same number. The ticket number is clearly written on the half-price pass number for future verification. One copy is given to the ticket purchaser for use.

Zhenzi Small Money Shop Yuanchang Mingji Closes Down 153

Promissory Notes Issued Temporarily Unpaid

The Closure of the Shop Has No Impact on Finance

Xin Sheng She reported that Shanghai money shops are divided into four levels: Yuan, Heng, Li, and Zhen. Yuanchang Mingji Money Shop, located at 74 Fujian Road, is a Zhenzi-level shop. It is small in scale, with a total capital of 15,000 yuan. The manager is Chen Shouchao. The address is at the intersection of Fujian Road and Guangdong Road, which is a one-room shop. It is not a member of the Money Industry Association. Although it issues promissory notes, it is actually equivalent to a tobacco and paper shop, exchanging silver coins and buying and selling securities for customers. It announced the suspension of business liquidation a few days ago due to financial difficulties.

Overdraft on Promissory Notes 154

It stopped business a few days ago and posted eight characters on the door: "Liquidation of Accounts, Notes Returned to Origin." A Xin Sheng She reporter learned from the shop yesterday that the reason for the financial difficulties and suspension of business liquidation was that the shop's deposits were gradually withdrawn by depositors. To date, the amount is only about 3,000 yuan. The promissory notes issued a few days ago amounted to about 8,000 yuan, which could not be paid temporarily, resulting in an overdraft.

Total Deposits 155

The shop's deposits are about 3,000 yuan, but the amount of loans is more than 3,000 yuan. Therefore, after the suspension of business, it was decided to liquidate according to law. After the loans are recovered, they will be returned to the depositors to ensure that the depositors do not suffer losses. Whether the business will resume in the future will depend on the shareholders' agreement. The closure of the shop has no impact on Shanghai's finance.
