National People's Credit Bureau Decides to Continue Operating as Usual Previous General Meeting Decided 157

Xin Sheng She reported that the National People's Credit Bureau, which was ordered to close down at the end of the year, has reached its deadline. It held a general meeting a few days ago and decided to continue operating until the government's settlement plan is announced. The post office has decided to stop delivering mail on its behalf. Details are as follows:

General Meeting of Representatives of National Credit Bureaus 158

The National People's Credit Bureau held a general meeting at the Credit Industry Association in Nanshi a few days ago. In addition to the seven general representatives from across the country, including Yin Yuantong, Hua Yunjin, Wang Dabao, Zhuang Gentang, Qiu Zhensheng, Ren Shiting, and Pan Wentian, all credit bureaus in Shanghai, such as Quansheng, Furunsong, Rizheng Xingkang, and Zhengdayuan, participated. The chairman reported on the progress, and then the discussion began. The meeting decided: (1) to continue operating until the government's settlement plan is announced; (2) if the General Post Office stops weighing and delivering credit bureau packages, it will resume the old method of delivering them itself; (3) to request the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to submit a request for relief to the central government.

Notice of Business and Request for Relief 159

In addition to notifying all national credit bureaus to follow the resolutions of the general meeting and continue operating as usual, the general representatives of the National People's Credit Bureau have also requested the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to submit a request for relief to the central government. It is now decided that all credit bureaus in Shanghai will operate as usual on the New Year's holidays of January 1st and 2nd, 1935, and will deliver special mail packages to the post office for weighing and delivery on the 3rd as usual. If the post office refuses, it will deliver them itself according to the old method to ensure that the mail is not delayed. The general representatives have also received instructions from the Ministry of Communications, rejecting the request to postpone the suspension of business.

Railway Temporarily Bans the Transport of Cattle Local Beef Panic Occurs 160

Price Rises from 14 Yuan to Nearly 20 Yuan

Foreigners Are the Most Affected

Since the discovery of foot-and-mouth disease in local cattle, the Municipal Health Bureau has submitted a request to the Municipal Government to consult the Ministry of Railways and request that the two railway bureaus be instructed to temporarily prohibit the loading of cattle for two weeks. The Health Bureau found that the infected cattle were first discovered at the Maigen Road Station. The cattle were loaded onto the railway from Benniu and Danyang stations. It is now known that the Ministry of Railways has instructed the two railway bureaus to do so. Therefore, there has been a great panic in the local cattle market, and the price of water buffalo meat has risen from 14 yuan to 19.6 yuan per dan, while the price of yellow beef has risen from 18 yuan to 24 yuan. At the same time, the import of cattle by water has also been greatly reduced due to the attention of the port quarantine office. Furthermore, a survey of the local cattle inventory shows that it is definitely not enough for two weeks of demand. As a result of supply falling short of demand, a beef shortage is inevitable. Foreigners who cannot swallow anything but beef are particularly affected.

Case of Selling Land and Excavating Ancestral Graves 161

Qian Liangzhou Does Not Know the Names of His Ancestors

But Claims That the Feng Shui Is Bad and Must Be Relocated

Qian Liangzhou, a 47-year-old native of Shanghai who lives in the Qianjia House on Talas Road in the French Concession and works as a vegetable vendor, and Qian Jianwen, a 62-year-old resident of the same house who used to be a local bailiff and now makes a living by farming, share an ancestral grave located in the second map of the 27th Bao of the upper town (i.e., Talas Road), with an area of more than four fen of land. Recently, Jianwen and his two sons, Qian Shunfa and Qian Jizhi, secretly made an agreement to sell the graveyard land to Zhu Zhensheng from Dongting Mountain. Liangzhou learned of this and tried to stop it, but to no avail. He hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the Civil Court of the Second Special Court, requesting confirmation that the ancestral graveyard base was the common property of all branches of the family and could not be privately moved or sold. After hearing the case, the court ruled that Qian Jianwen should not privately move the jointly owned ancestral grave. However, after the verdict, Qian Jianwen expressed his dissatisfaction and filed an appeal. On the morning of the 5th of this month, he gathered 20 workers at the site and excavated the ancestral grave. Liangzhou learned of this and invited his clansmen Qian Jisheng and Qian Guisheng to stop him, but to no avail. The two sides then went to the Shanzhong Road French Police Station. After reporting the incident, the head of the police ordered Jianwen to make a pledge to stop excavating the graves. However, after leaving the police station, Jianwen continued to supervise the workers in excavating the graves, unearthing the coffins, collecting the bones, and burying them elsewhere. Qian Liangzhou and others then filed another complaint with the police station, requesting that they be detained and investigated. At that time, the police ordered them to file a lawsuit in the court. At this point, Qian Liangzhou, Qian Jisheng, and Qian Guisheng took photos of the excavated graveyard and collected evidence such as coffin fragments and bones. They hired a lawyer to file a self-accusation with the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court in accordance with Articles 263, 265, 337, and 356 of the Criminal Law, accusing Qian Jianwen, Qian Shunfa, Qian Jizhi, and the middleman Zhu Zhensheng, Huang Miaojin, of destroying graves, seizing public property, and stealing treasures from the graves, and requesting that they be investigated and dealt with according to law. The court granted the request and once held a hearing. Only Zhu and Huang appeared, while Qian Jianwen and his sons did not report. They were instructed to reschedule the hearing. The details have been briefly reported in the newspaper. The day before yesterday, Judge Qiu Huan-ying summoned them again in the Second Criminal Court. The plaintiffs and their lawyers arrived and stated the previous situation. They also brought the coffin fragments and scattered bones wrapped in red paper as evidence. The defendants Qian Jianwen, Zhu Zhensheng, and Huang Miaojin, along with their defense lawyers, appeared, but Qian Shunfa and Qian Jizhi did not. According to Qian Jianwen's statement, the ancestral grave was inherited from my ancestors and contains the remains of the eighth-generation ancestors, with a total of eight coffins. Because the Qian family has been unlucky for many years, with frequent illnesses, a feng shui master was consulted who said that the feng shui of the ancestral grave was bad. Therefore, on the 5th of this month, the grave was moved and buried in the cemetery west of Hongqiao on December 23rd. It was sold to the Zhu family in June for a total price of 6,200 yuan. This graveyard is not the public property of the plaintiffs. The official asked, "What are the names of the ancestors buried in the grave? Who are they to you?" Jianwen stared blankly and could not answer, claiming, "I am illiterate, I don't know. But I have a copy of the inscription on the stone tablet, which I handed over to the lawyer." The official also asked, "Why are your sons Shunfa and Jiji not here today?" He replied, "This matter was my own decision and has nothing to do with my sons. My sons were not at the scene when the grave was moved. Both of my sons have businesses and don't have time to come." The official said, "As a defendant in a lawsuit, you should come to court. You cannot resist and not come. If you do not come without a reason, this court will issue a warrant for your arrest." Jianwen listened to the instructions and said, "I can call my sons to come to court next time." According to Zhu Zhensheng's statement, I bought this land in June for 16,000 yuan. Huang Miaojin was the middleman. I didn't know it was public ancestral property at first. I only saw a tomb on the ground and didn't know how many coffins were buried underground. The middleman Huang Miaojin admitted to being a witness. I was not at the scene when the grave was demolished. The official then asked the plaintiffs what they meant by accusing Zhu Zhensheng and Huang Miaojin. Qian Liangzhou replied, "They knew that this graveyard was public property and colluded to buy and sell it privately. Although Zhu Zhensheng was not at the scene when the grave was excavated, the middleman Huang Miaojin was at the scene helping to remove the boundary stones." At this point, the official, as the defendants were not all present, instructed that the hearing be rescheduled for January 7, 1935, and instructed Qian Jianwen to bring Qian Shunfa and Qian Jiji to court next time. Failure to do so would result in their arrest.

Lawsuit Between Mother and Son of Former Manager of Ziyang Temple Zhao Zhixuan Resolved 162

Lu Cuixia Wins

After the death of Zhao Zhixuan, the former manager of Ziyang Temple, a family dispute arose. His son, Zhao Futang, did not recognize his stepmother, Zhao Lu Cuixia, and filed a criminal self-accusation against Zhao Lu for embezzlement in the Second Special Court. Zhao Lu hired lawyer Cai Liucheng to defend her. Recently, the court ruled that she was indeed Zhao Zhixuan's stepmother and dismissed Zhao Futang's self-accusation. Zhao Futang and his daughter-in-law, Zhao Huang, then sued her uncle, Lu Shutang, for theft. Lu Shutang also hired lawyer Cai to defend him and filed a counterclaim for injury. Lu Shutang was acquitted. Zhao Futang and Zhao Huang were jointly sentenced to two months of imprisonment for injuring someone's body, both with a two-year suspended sentence. Zhao Futang also filed a complaint with the French Concession police station accusing his stepmother of theft, but his stepmother was also acquitted. At the same time, Zhao Futang also sued his stepmother in the civil court, requesting the return of the title deeds, etc., but his request was also rejected.

Ke Yinghao Accused of Rent Arrears Suddenly Claims Japanese Nationality 163

Intending to Resist Legal Sanctions

Judge Orders Him to Provide Sufficient Proof

Ke Yinghao, a Cantonese, previously rented a house at No. 5 Pingle Lane, Xizang Road, from Liu Yide's rental agency for a monthly rent of 125.87 yuan. Since May of this year, he has delayed paying the rent, accumulating arrears of over eight months, totaling 1,006.96 yuan. After repeated requests were unsuccessful, the rental agency hired lawyer Zhu Sifu to file a lawsuit in the Civil Court of the First Special District, accusing Ke of rent arrears and demanding full payment. Yesterday, Judge Luo Chongtai of the First Special Court summoned Ke Yinghao in the Seventh Civil Court. When the bailiff served the summons, Ke Yinghao suddenly claimed to be of Japanese nationality and did not appear in court. Lawyer Zhu Sifu immediately stated that the defendant Ke Yinghao is actually Cantonese. He did not declare his Japanese nationality when renting the house. Now that the case has occurred, he suddenly claims to be of Japanese nationality, clearly intending to rely on the power of a foreign national to resist the judgment of our country's laws. However, according to our country's laws, any citizen who renounces citizenship must obtain a renunciation certificate from the Ministry of Interior. Since the defendant claims to be of Japanese nationality, he should be ordered by the court to present the renunciation certificate from the Ministry of Interior and the certificate of Japanese citizenship to prove it. Otherwise, the court should make a judgment according to law. Judge Luo examined the ticket and instructed that the case be rescheduled for trial on January 10th of next year and ordered the defendant to provide sufficient proof of whether he has already renounced his citizenship. The court was then adjourned.

Newspaper Reporters Association Aids Chongmin Daily Reporter 164

Telegraph to Jiangsu Provincial Government Requesting Impartial Investigation

The Shanghai Newspaper Reporters Association, on the 28th of this month, received an urgent letter from the Chongming Chongmin Daily and the New Chongming Review, stating that Lu Ping, the main contributor to the Review, had been illegally detained by Wang Bin, the county magistrate of the county. They requested assistance. The Reporters Association convened a meeting of its standing committee on the 29th and decided to send a telegram to the Jiangsu Provincial Government requesting an impartial investigation. The original telegram is as follows: "To the Honorable Yu, Head of the Civil Affairs Department of Jiangsu Province, Zhenjiang. Our association has received a letter from the Chongming Chongmin Daily and the New Chongming Review, stating that Lu Ping, a reporter for this newspaper and main contributor to the New Chongming Review, has been illegally detained by Wang Bin, the county magistrate of this county, for five days. We request your upholding of justice and providing assistance. We have found that Lu Ping, a reporter for this newspaper, is a man of integrity and chivalry, who has served the press for six or seven years. He is usually forthright and upright, upholds public opinion, and works diligently for the welfare of the local people. He is praised by the villagers. Recently, in view of the corruption in local politics in this county, the rulers sell official titles, engage in bribery and corruption, and plunder the people's wealth without any restraint. Therefore, he published a new type of Chongming Review to eradicate traitors and filth, criticize evil policies, engage in the national rejuvenation movement, and promote the Three Principles of the People. Since its publication, it has been well received by society. However, it was resented by County Magistrate Wang Bin and his henchmen, who often thought of destroying it, but could not find an excuse. On the morning of the 19th of this month, Lu Ping heard that the provincial government ordered the Nantong Commissioner's Office to instruct the county government to detain Zhang Ji, the former chief of the general affairs section, and Zhao Chengxin, the chief of the investigation section, of the county's anti-smoking committee, who were colluding in corruption, and send them to the province. Zhang Ji, fearing punishment, fled. He then interviewed Wang Bin, the county magistrate, who was also the chairman of the anti-smoking committee, and asked if the news was true. Wang Bin used this news to spread it to the outside world, making it difficult to escape suspicion of being involved in the same wrongdoing. He falsely accused the article 'Novel Commemorative Week' in the New Chongming Review of insulting administrative officials and detained Lu to silence him. He was initially detained in the political police office for six hours before the court opened and Wang personally interrogated him. In the name of interrogation, he only asked about his name, age, and other things, and then sent him to the detention center without saying a word. It has been five days. Wang Bin is using his power to illegally detain a sacred newspaper reporter out of personal grudges, treating the law as waste paper and disregarding public reason. Under the central government's clear order to protect the safety of newspaper reporters, how can we tolerate this county magistrate who disregards the law and acts recklessly in broad daylight? Lu Ping is innocent and has been unjustly imprisoned. He is in prison and lacks the power and influence to defend himself. In order to save the unfortunate Lu Ping and to fight for the freedom of newspaper reporters, we have to ask your association to uphold justice and provide assistance. Not only will Lu Ping be grateful, but our press will also be fortunate," etc. It is clearly stipulated in the Provisional Constitution during the period of political tutelage that the people's freedom of speech and personal freedom should be protected. Whether the case of Chongming County Magistrate detaining Lu Ping involves illegal acts of resentment, we request your office to investigate the matter thoroughly and handle it impartially in accordance with the law. This is our hope. Shanghai Newspaper Reporters Association, respectfully, 30th Seal."

Second Asylum for the Poor Opens Today 165

The Shanghai Charity Association's Hunan Asylum, located in the Chaozhou Guild Hall at the South Railway Station, has already accommodated more than 1,300 poor people and is already full. Some of the poor people, suffering from not being able to be placed, are emaciated and sleeping outside the gate. The chairman, Wang Yiting, and Huang Hanzhi, were heartbroken when they saw this and have been running around for days seeking help from the authorities. Yang, the director of the security team stationed at the Chao Huishan Villa on Xietu Road, has ordered them to move out. Therefore, the second asylum has been preparing for days and was completed yesterday. A notice was issued stating that it would be established today and begin to take in people. It is expected that the poor people who come to the asylum will be able to obtain food and shelter to get through the New Year. The staff of the second asylum has been announced, including Mao Jianqing, Xu Tianxi, Lu Jiyu, Shi Zhaishan, Wang Diyuan, Ye Ziwei, Xu Shaoting, etc. The letter from the asylum to the Public Security Bureau is as follows: "Respectfully, our asylum is now setting up a second asylum at the Chao Huishan Villa on Xietu Road and is scheduled to begin taking in people on the 30th of this month. We are writing to inform you and respectfully request that your bureau instruct all sub-bureaus to send any homeless poor people they find to our asylum for accommodation, etc."

Longevity Gift Transferred to Scholarship Fund 166

Mother of Jiaotong University Teacher Chen Huaishu

The mother of Mr. Chen Huaishu, a teacher at Jiaotong University, Madam Liu, will celebrate her 80th birthday on January 8th next year. Relatives and friends originally planned to celebrate it, but Madam declined it repeatedly due to the current national crisis. Mr. Chen also believes that it is now a time to practice a new life and advocates simplicity in everything. Therefore, following the advice of relatives and friends, he abolished all superficial formalities, collected the longevity gifts, added them to the banquet funds, and transferred them all to the Jiaotong University Scholarship Fund to cultivate promising students.

Cattle and Sheep Industry Association Sends Letters to Various Places to Pay Attention to Sick Cattle 167

Henceforth, Cattle Arriving in Shanghai Will Not Be Sick

Since the Health Bureau banned cattle from arriving in Shanghai for two weeks due to foot-and-mouth disease in cattle arriving recently, the cattle merchants petitioned for six alternative measures to be approved. It is now reported that the industry association has sent letters to cattle dealers and cattle brokers in Nanjing, Danyang, Changzhou, Hangzhou, and Xuzhou and Bengbu in northern Jiangsu, prohibiting them from purchasing and transporting cattle with foot-and-mouth disease to Shanghai. They also informed all parties of the morphology of foot-and-mouth disease in the Health Bureau's instructions for identification. Then the foot-and-mouth disease in cattle arriving in Shanghai should soon be eradicated.

Kneeling Petition Group Kneels to Persuade University Students 168

Students Are at the Forefront of the National Goods Year

Shiye News reports: Since its establishment, the National Soul Kneeling Petition Group, organized by patriotic youths Wang Hanchun and others in this city, has been working extremely hard on kneeling petitions. People from all walks of life, feeling the patriotic sincerity of the group members, expressed their sympathy. Even those who accidentally purchased foreign goods would immediately repent after being knelt to by the group. Yesterday, Wang and other members of the group met three university students near the Dananmen on Zhonghua Road. They were all wearing wool uniforms, and one of them held several books of foreign paper stationery. Wang, seeing them approaching, immediately shouted, "Are you Chinese or foreigners?" They were stunned when they heard this. Wang then stepped forward and knelt down, saying, "You are the masters of the country, and you bear a great responsibility. How can you wear foreign wool and write on foreign paper stationery? Isn't that even more heartbreaking? Now I (Wang referring to himself) sincerely persuade you to use national goods and save the country together." They were greatly ashamed when they heard this, expressed their repentance, and tore up the stationery to show their determination. Wang was satisfied and returned.

Famous cartoonists Huang Shiying and Huang Ding are outstanding talents in the Chinese cartoon world. Their works are deeply appreciated by readers. Annual Meeting of the Belgian Alumni Association Today 171

There are many Chinese students who have studied in Belgium in the past. Most of them serve in Beijing, Shanghai, Tianjin and other places. This year's annual meeting is scheduled to be held at 2:00 p.m. today at the association's clubhouse on Lafayette Road. Letter to the Editor 172

To the Editor: I recently read an article in the news column of your newspaper on the 28th, titled "Police Chief Opens Fire Out of Grudge," the facts of which are completely fabricated. I, the undersigned, only started working at the Yangjiadu Police Station after the January 28th Incident. At that time, the shop owner, Gong Jinlin, was insane and selling enemy goods. I advised him with righteous words, but he retorted with arrogance and was shameless. Then he received a large batch of small goods, which were investigated by the River and Sea Customs' Ship Management Office's Water Patrol Police, who seized the loot, causing him to hate me to the bone and intend to frame me. On the afternoon of the 27th, the local court summoned us for a clear confrontation. The prosecutor refuted Gong Jinlin's fabrication on the spot. The previous report damaged my reputation. I am writing to you specifically to request a correction. Sincerely, Wu Tianzhi, 158 Yangjiadu, Pudong, December 30th.

Editor's Note

The Most Tragic Year for This Newspaper 176

— Tingchen

Since Mr. Shi Liangcai took over this newspaper in the first year of the Republic of China, after more than 20 years of hard work and the unremitting efforts of colleagues, it has reached its current position. I have always been comforted by this, following my colleagues. Unexpectedly, this year, not long after the New Year, an unfortunate incident occurred. On February 26th, Mr. Qin Liqi, the English translator, died of stomach illness in his Shanghai residence. Colleagues deeply mourned Qin's loyalty to his duties and his overwork. Unexpectedly, after just over 60 days, his wife, Ms. Gong Yinxia, and her daughters, Xisun, eldest son Duan, and second son Jue, all took medicine at midnight on May 5th. The next morning, they followed Mr. Qin to the underworld, and the whole family died for righteousness. Opinion was divided among contemporary commentators, but all the colleagues of this newspaper could not help but shed tears of sympathy. The museum sent staff to manage the funeral and hired Mr. Zhang Yunhe to go to Xichang to pay his respects and discuss funeral matters with Mr. Pingfu, Qin's elderly father. See Mr. Yunhe's "Visiting Friends in Xichang" in the June 1st Free Talk. This is a tragedy. This year, there was a severe drought in the summer and the weather was extremely hot. The highest temperature reached 104 degrees, breaking the Observatory's 60-year record. Colleagues were celebrating their good fortune and safe passage, but on October 23rd, Mr. Hu Juru, the accountant, suddenly died of a minor illness. Mr. Hu was just over sixty years old. Although he was physically weak, he was gentle in nature and had a comfortable family background. If there had been no unexpected stimulation, he would have been able to live out his natural life. Unfortunately, he had a son in his later years, who suddenly died of illness. His wife cried excessively and soon died. She was pregnant at the time of death. Mr. Hu, in addition to mourning the loss of his son, also composed elegies for his deceased wife. He was suffering from illness and died suddenly the day after his wife's funeral. Mr. Hu's family of four deaths is different from Mr. Qin's family of five deaths, but the tragedy is the same. This is another tragedy. Mr. Hu passed away when Mr. Shi had gone to Hangzhou for recuperation. When the obituary arrived in Hangzhou, he immediately sent a letter to Mr. Yunhe, saying, "Another old friend of Shenbao has become weaker." The implication was that he could not help but sigh. Unexpectedly, two weeks later, like a bolt from the blue, suddenly and unexpectedly, Mr. Shi was murdered by bandits on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway at 2:00 p.m. on November 13th. At 6:00 p.m., the police report arrived at the museum. Colleagues were shocked when they heard the bad news and suspected that the messenger was lying. After confirmation, the tragic situation at that time left a deep impression forever. After the shock calmed down, the staff of this museum and the Shi family made some arrangements and rushed to Hangzhou overnight to meet the remains. They arrived at the mansion the next afternoon. The coffin was placed on the 16th. The entire staff of this newspaper held a memorial service at the Lake Society on December 8th. 491 people attended. The atmosphere at the meeting was extremely solemn. This is the unprecedented tragedy since the founding of this newspaper. In the past ten years, colleagues of this newspaper have died one after another. Recalling the past, the book and sword drifted away, and their voices and appearances are still there. Thinking of the old grass, there is endless sorrow. For example, Mr. Pei Guoxiong died of typhoid fever, Mr. Dai Yisun died of consumptive disease, Mr. Xie Jiezi died of peritonitis, and Mr. Kang Tongyi died of pneumonia. When they died, I always wrote about their illnesses and their deeds and published them in the newspaper. Every time I wrote, I was always moved to tears. Whenever I thought of orphans and widows, I could not help but sigh. However, the above gentlemen mostly died of illness, and there were several years between them. There has never been a year like this year, one after another, in addition to dying of illness, there are also those who committed suicide and were killed. "Life has come to this, how can the heavens be discussed? I hate people, and I am terrified." When I read Jiang Wentong's Hate Fu, I could not help but put down my book and sigh. I am writing this here, and there is another painful thing that I must attach and write to express my worries. In the second year of the Xuantong era, I left the Zhongwai Daily. In the third year of the Xuantong era, Mr. He Caitang introduced me to Mr. Dong Xipei, the former East seat of this newspaper. Later, I was not abandoned by Mr. Shi and continued to serve until now for more than 20 years. However, Mr. He died of lung disease on November 3rd, ten days before Mr. Shi, and returned to the mountains. (For Mr. He's deeds, see the December 10th Three Groups Memorial Service article in this newspaper.) Within a year, relatives and friends withered away. I mourned the old friends and cried for my personal relatives. How can I not be sad? In the past, Xiang Xiu thought about the past and Lu Ji lamented the passing of time. Even the thatched hut had old friends visiting and exclaiming, and sad poems. Who has no feelings? Who can get rid of this? Especially when I have personally experienced it. How many times have I seen the destruction of sesame trees? How can I dare to sigh for orchids? I also just express my sorrow.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise 179

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 7: Hearing the words, she covers her tears and sells herself to tell of her bitterness; carefully spying, she presents an invitation card with ardent affection.

Jia Duocai said, "The matter of taking a concubine, what is the rush? It's just that, I just chased them away, I'm afraid they'll be offended." Li Shilian smiled and said, "If it's for this matter, then it's easy to handle. Just now I saw them go to the tea room, Little Ji's place. Maybe they haven't left yet. I'll go and mention it to them and let them come back." Jia Duocai smiled and cupped his hands twice, saying, "I wouldn't dare, and this matter can't be decided in just a few words. We should take our time. If we rush, I'm afraid they'll be pretentious." Li Shilian was seeking his help, so he naturally didn't dare to disobey his wishes. Upon hearing this, he immediately changed his attitude, stopped moving, and smiled at him, "That's fine too. We'll talk about it in a couple of days. You can't indulge women too much. Once you do, they'll put on airs." Jia Duocai, hearing this, felt awkward. He first took a puff of a cigarette, then tilted his head slightly and thought for a while. He supported the cigarette with one hand and touched his cheek with the other, swayed his body twice, and smiled, "If they haven't left, maybe they're waiting for my reply. If I don't give them a reply, they won't know how long to wait. How about... asking the tea room attendant to check on the situation?" Li Shilian smiled and said, "That's not appropriate. The tea room attendants are all in cahoots with them. They'll tell you whatever you want to hear. You can't get any real information that way. I should go." Jia Duocai then smiled and patted his shoulder, saying, "It's good for you to go. Please handle the matter well. If you have the chance, you might as well negotiate with them." Li Shilian patted his chest and said, "Leave the matter to me. I will definitely convince them." But since you are taking a concubine, Brother Jia, this is a matter of enjoyment. You always have to spend some money for happiness. If they have some small requests, you might as well accommodate them a little. Besides, someone like Brother Jia in the banking industry wouldn't care about that." As he said this, he also raised his hand and patted Jia Duocai's shoulder. Only then did he walk towards the backyard with a smile. He saw through Jia Duocai's attitude. He was determined to marry this girl. If he succeeded as a matchmaker and pleased him, perhaps he would repay this kindness and find a good opportunity for me. (103)

Painted Faces 180

— Wubian

"Painted faces" are a specialized art of actors. Actors put in painstaking effort and go through elaborate procedures for the skill of painting faces. They follow the script and never neglect it because whether the painted face is realistic or not is closely related to the atmosphere of the performance and gaining the audience's emotions of joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness. For example, in the stage, with one look you know the wicked and treacherous, the loyal and virtuous. At the same time, to show sympathy and resonance, the painted face accounts for a large part of the power to reveal. Therefore, those learning to be actors, no old master withholds the teaching of the "face painting manual" and the actors do not fail to learn it.

In fact, "painted faces" is no longer an exclusive art or unique skill of actors. In this society, all ordinary humans, especially the extraordinary people, have this set of artistic skills. However, actors’ painted faces have the guidance of an old master, are based on a face painting manual, and are touched up with colors. Therefore, this kind of painted face is dead, a stereotypical version. Unlike the painted faces of ordinary and extraordinary people, which are alive and adaptable. Because the painted faces of us ordinary and extraordinary people have no guidance from an old master, nor a face painting manual as a basis, we rely entirely on our ability to make inferences and comprehend. Therefore, we do not need to use colors to touch up, and what is expressed and revealed is often more powerful and effective than those touched up with colors. The painted face of an ordinary person is naturally more ordinary in power and effect. However, extraordinary people who paint extraordinary faces must go through a stage of ordinary people painting ordinary faces. In other words, one must first be an ordinary person painting an ordinary face before one can reach the point of an extraordinary person painting an extraordinary face. However, this is not for those who are stupid or dull-witted.

In this society, it can truly be said that the use of painted faces is great. Let me give you a rough idea: all high officials and nobles, Western-style houses and cars, gold and beauties, as well as all kinds of pleasant titles such as "master" can be exchanged for the face that is painted. For example, when you see a ×× and a beggar at the same time, why do you respect the ×× but despise the beggar? It is because the ×× can paint faces, but the beggar cannot.

The use of "painted faces" is great indeed in this society.

Morning at the Bund Park 182

— Yunshang

Occasionally, one morning, I woke up early while it was still somewhat dark and hurriedly stepped into the Bund Park along the Huangpu River.

At this time, not only could you not encounter any tourists in the park, but even the little birds in the trees were still sound asleep. The rows of old trees on the pavement had all lost their leaves, and the outstretched branches appeared very thin and weak. The chrysanthemums had long been taken away by the winter wind, leaving only a patch of withered yellow grass still wearing the dew from last night, emitting patches of sparkling light. The Huangpu River was quiet, and the river surface was covered in a mist like light smoke. Looking out, you could not distinguish between the water and the sky, and with a few small steamboats vaguely wriggling in the thick fog, it was even more like a traditional ink painting.

Before long, the scenery suddenly changed. The large morning sun, draped in a red robe, shone with ten thousand rays of light, revealing half of its face in the eastern corner. Those ten thousand rays of golden light scattered the smoke and mist covering the Jiangnan region, and the river water instantly glowed. All the houses, factory chimneys, and forests across the river appeared in clear outline. And looking back at the Bund Garden, it was also dotted with light. A seagull, carrying the sunlight faster than an arrow, skimmed across the river surface, just like the poet praised: "How beautiful! The morning of life, how joyous! The morning of life." The feeling made one receive the morning sun's infinite grace.

Everything seemed to wake up from a deep sleep. The lonely air suddenly became very lively. The whistles of the small steamboats on the Huangpu River were calling, and the wheels of the trams on the road were also calling. The little birds in the trees were singing even more sweetly and movingly. Amidst the calls, many tourists had already come in one after another, some strolling, some practicing boxing, some taking deep breaths. They were probably all "hygienists," right?

At this time, the Bund Park was very lively.

Records of Fleeting Fragrance 184

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Chapter 20: Shooting Range

The Empress Dowager's purpose in visiting the east this time was primarily to tour the scenic spots and historical sites in and around Fengtian City, with no political implications whatsoever. Therefore, after visiting the Fox Immortal Pagoda, she also decided to visit the shooting range where the rulers of the Qing Dynasty used to practice archery and horsemanship before entering the pass. (The so-called shooting range is also a hunting ground. However, according to numerous inquiries by the translator, this shooting range should be in Dongling, Fengtian, and the area is very small, which is different from what is said here. Other than that, there are no fixed hunting grounds in Fengtian! So, the plot described in this chapter is probably fabricated by the author herself; however, some of the anecdotes are indeed true.) The location of this shooting range was about northwest of Fengtian City. The journey from the Shengjing Palace was very long, and it would take a lot of time to get there by sedan chair. Its area was very vast, about ten or twenty li square. Half of it was forest, and the trees in the forest were mostly tall, evergreen trees, so the shade was extremely dense. In the mountainous areas around Fengtian, such large forests were not uncommon and could be seen almost everywhere: unlike in the provinces of the Central Plains, where larger trees were cut down for fuel, and it was no longer possible to form any forests.

The history of this shooting range is indeed extremely long! Before the strength of our Manchu part of the Chinese nation had become strong, that is, before unifying China, when it was just a remote border tribe, it already existed importantly. (213)

Those Skilled at Blaming Others 185

— (Xu Xiaoting)

A judge who already has a legal wife still marries a concubine and tries a bigamy case in his court. In a certain sense, he can very well understand the judgment of the national law he should receive.

Romantic young men who frequent brothels and sleep with prostitutes are the strictest in guarding their wives. In a certain period, they can be the most attentive in questioning.

People who believe in Buddhism often say that those who believe in Christianity are too superstitious. Conversely, Christians also hold the same view of Buddhists.

A chauffeur goes to court for running over a pedestrian. He does not blame himself for not being careful, but scolds the dead person for running too slowly.

An engineer contracts to build a house. He does not prepare solid building materials. Once the house is built and collapses, he blames the soil under the house's foundation for being too poor.

A contributor whose submitted manuscript is not published does not blame his own writing for being too bad, but blames the editor for having poor eyesight.

Small Knowledge

Common Knowledge of Winter Clothes 186

— Bingyu

From a health perspective, coarse but soft cotton fabrics are most suitable for underwear (shirts), but this varies depending on the season and climate. Now that winter has arrived, one should understand the basic knowledge of clothing, that is, what is the nature of the material of the clothes worn, and what is its relationship with the body? The texture of ordinary clothes is divided into two types: planar warp and weft elasticity, and three-dimensional thick elasticity. Three-dimensional thick elasticity is compressive elasticity, and its texture's insulation and air content are closely related. However, there are differences due to the elasticity of the fibers themselves, the texture of the structure, and the direction in which the fibers and threads run. Wool, camel hair, and other woolen fabrics are rich in insulation, while linen and silk have very little. Therefore, summer clothes are made of linen and winter clothes are made of fur. However, within the same raw material, those with coarse textures and woven-like appearances, whose lines run in a more angular direction on the surface of the texture, or are fluffy, and those with fluff, are richer in compressive elasticity. Now, carefully investigating the texture of clothing, very little air is left in the gaps inside. Even if woven with a very dense method, the air content is mostly above 40%, and usually between 6% and 8%. Extremely coarse and fluffy flannel contains 90% air, so materials with compressive elasticity must have a lot of air content. When our bodies reach winter, because the temperature of the outside air is lower than the body temperature, the body temperature is taken away by the outside air, and we feel cold. If the air temperature drops to 15 degrees, our hands and feet will freeze. At this time, measuring the temperature inside the clothes with a thermometer, the body temperature is 36.5 degrees, the surface of woolen underwear is 28.5 degrees, and the surface of outerwear is 19.4 degrees. Therefore, wearing more clothes in winter gradually changes the temperature, with outerwear being lower than mid-layers, and mid-layers being lower than underwear. The insulating material of underwear has a great relationship with skin temperature. Why? Originally, the clothes we wear do not have warmth themselves, but are warmed by the air held within the clothes. Clothes are like the walls of a house. Underwear with wide collars and sleeves easily loses skin temperature. Therefore, the most important thing for winter underwear is to be close to the skin, have little heat transfer, and have little air permeability, making it difficult to dissipate temperature. It is best to wear thermal underwear, flannel underwear, and woolen sweaters for insulation. Among heat-transferring materials, ramie and silk are the greatest, while wool and flannel are the least. However, being too close to the skin is very unhygienic. Why? Our skin constantly releases water vapor and carbon dioxide. If it is too close, it will cause obstacles and prevent the activity of bodily functions. Wearing wool, flannel, silk, and fur clothes in winter, because they are very rich in air content, allows body temperature to be slowly dissipated, and the air content inside the clothes has moisture, which has an insulating effect. This moisture absorbs moisture. Ramie and silk absorb moisture quickly and release moisture quickly, so they also quickly take away body temperature. Woolen fabrics and fur are the opposite, which is the principle of summer linen and winter fur. Recently, in cities, one often sees ignorant fools who lack common sense and think they are modern wearing silk as winter underwear to show off their wealth, but in fact, they are despised for exposing their lack of common knowledge about clothing. Furthermore, the raw materials of clothing textures, as mentioned above, must have rich air content, little air permeability, and moisture. However, the fiber type of the raw material, the weaving method, and the thickness of the weave are very important. Materials woven with fibers in a smooth direction are most prone to heat transfer and air permeability. Coarse-woven fabrics (such as gauze sold in pharmacies) are suitable for making underwear because they have compressive elasticity and can insulate.

The Xuhui Huaguang Team held a 15,600-meter long-distance race yesterday morning. A total of 50 people registered in advance, but only 42 registered at the time of the race. New House Completed at Qingdao National Arts Hall ▲ Ceremony and Performance of National Arts Held ▲ Shen Honglie Visited and Gave a Speech 193

Qingdao Newsletter, Qingdao National Arts Hall was established in the Republic of China in 18. Through the promotion of successive authorities, it has achieved today's achievements. There are as many as 95 National Arts practice centers in the city, with more than 5,000 practitioners. A total of more than 3,000 people have graduated. Recently, a women's practice center has been established to provide equal development opportunities for men and women's national arts. With this gradual promotion, there will be considerable progress in a few years. Mayor and National Arts Hall Director Shen Honglie, due to the lack of a location for the National Arts Hall, had many inconveniences in its implementation. Therefore, he allocated a government-owned land on Guangdong Road to build the National Arts Hall in the spring of this year. It was completed this winter, requiring a total of more than 16,000 yuan for construction costs and internal installation costs. In addition to Mayor Shen's donation of 3,000 yuan, the rest was donated by all sectors of society. On the morning of the 23rd of this month at 9:00 AM, a ceremony was held to celebrate the completion of the new house. Mayor Shen and representatives from various organizations attended, totaling hundreds of people. Mayor Shen presided over the ceremony, and then the secretary of the hall, Xiang Zongding, reported on the evolution of the National Arts Hall. Mayor Shen then delivered a speech, followed by a speech by Li Xianliang, a member of the city party. The performance of national arts then began, and the ceremony was completed and dismissed after 12:00 noon. The secretary's report and Mayor Shen's speech are recorded separately below.

▲ History of the National Arts Hall 194

Briefly stated, this hall was established in the 18th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1929]. Initially, it used the reception room of Yuying Primary School as a temporary office. Later, it moved to Ling County Road, and then to Shanghe Road. All these moves were due to the small size of the premises, which hindered development. At first, one instructor class was set up, with a half-year graduation period. Subsequently, practice classes were recruited, which were of a mobile nature. From the 19th year [1930] onwards, practice centers were gradually established and expanded, now reaching as many as 95. Currently, about 2,000 people are practicing in these centers, and about 3,000 have graduated. That year, a wrestling class was also established, because wrestling has equal value to boxing. Wrestling in this city was very rudimentary, and there was indeed a need to promote it. Approximately 300 people have graduated so far. In addition, the issue of examining and certifying national arts education is also extremely important. In October of the 21st year [1932], the first examination was held, with 82 people passing. In December of the 22nd year [1933], the second examination was held, with 103 people passing. Furthermore, in June of the 20th year [1931], in accordance with the regulations of the Central National Arts Hall, the first city examination was held, selecting 14 martial artists. In July of the 21st year [1932], the second city examination was held, selecting 15 martial artists. Regarding the hall's participation in various sports meets, in the 19th year [1930], representatives were sent to Hangzhou to participate in the national arts examination. In the same year, a national arts competition was held in Shanghai, and the hall also sent personnel to participate. In the 21st year [1932], the 16th North China Games were held in Henan, and the hall sent four representatives to participate. In the 22nd year [1933], the 17th North China Games were held in Qingdao, along with the National Games of the same year, and this year's 18th North China Games, all achieving good results and winning the 18th championship. Regarding the hall's finances, when it was first established, the municipal government subsidized 300 yuan per month, which was very tight at the time. In the 20th year [1931], it was increased to 500 yuan per month, but it was still not enough to cover expenses. In the 22nd year [1933], Mayor Shen approved an increase to 600 yuan per month. Since July of last year, the municipal government has increased the hall's funding, allocating 300 yuan every three months for rewarding the various practice centers. The practice centers are inspected once every three months, with the best being rewarded and the worst being shut down. Last year, the municipal government also requested a temporary allocation of 1,000 yuan, and the hall's colleagues donated 100 yuan to buy 500 broadswords and manufacture other weapons. Moreover, physical education for both men and women is equally important. A women's practice class was established in July of last year, with more than 30 people. Recently, a women's practice center was established and has already begun recruiting students, aiming to simultaneously advance national arts for both men and women. This is the general situation of the hall since its establishment. Recalling the simplicity of the past, now residing in this magnificent building, there has indeed been progress compared to the past. However, this is only a superficial matter. As for national arts itself, how to promote it, how to expand it, the hall's colleagues will naturally follow the mayor's intentions and the guidance of all sectors to strive forward.

▲ Admonition by Shen Honglie 195

Briefly stated, the municipal national arts hall has indeed made progress in the past five years, with significant improvements in both knowledge and skills. However, amidst this joy, I feel a sense of crisis, because the municipal national arts hall has dominated various sports meets, winning too many championships. The 18th North China Games almost became a monopoly for our city, and I fear that this will lead to arrogance and a decline in skills. This is the danger that I feel. We should not be arrogant, nor should we be discouraged. Only by constantly striving can we make progress. I would like to take this opportunity to explain the goals for promoting physical education, which can be divided into three categories: (1) Popularization: Whether it be organizations, schools, or the public, everyone should have physical education, and physical education should be rationalized. New physical education and old physical education should be integrated. Whether it be Boy Scouts, military training, ball games, or track and field events, they should all be made into rationalized physical education. Therefore, the implementation methods should not make physical education a temporary subject but should make it a required course. Standards have already been drafted and will definitely be implemented in the future. All organizations, groups, and factories should organize various sports teams, such as basketball teams, volleyball teams, or national arts teams. After forming these teams, they should compete frequently to promote progress. As for the public, various sports should be added to the people's schools so that everyone has the opportunity to practice. By doing so, popularization can be gradually achieved. (2) Excellence: Schools and groups should be made to compete frequently, and then excellent individuals should be selected from each group and trained, which will surely lead to good results. (3) Unity: Whether it be track and field, ball games, boxing, wrestling, military training, Boy Scout training, or even skating, horse racing, kite flying, and shuttlecock kicking, they should all be integrated. Techniques should be practiced interdependently, without distinction between fields, so that an entire group can be formed. Only by striving to implement these three things can we truly promote physical education and naturally cultivate healthy citizens. As for championships, they are merely matters for after-dinner conversation. We do not hope for them. This is my general policy for promoting physical education.

Ministry of Education Donates Siku Quanshu to Libraries in Various European Countries 200

The rare edition of the Siku Quanshu of China was previously printed by the Commercial Press, totaling more than 230 types and more than 3,000 volumes, to be completed in four phases by the end of next year. The first phase has now been published. For the purpose of international exchange and cultural communication, the Ministry of Education, after consultations with various parties, has decided to donate one copy to each of eight famous libraries in various European countries. On the 29th, it also consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to inform the embassies of the respective European countries to be gifted, so as to gradually send the published rare editions of the Siku Quanshu.

Ministry of Education Compiles "The Current Status of Chinese Education" 201

The Ministry of Education has conducted annual surveys on higher education, secondary education, and social education, and has compiled various statistics. However, each department prints its own booklets, and there is no relatively concrete and comprehensive publication. Now, for international exchange and domestic application, the Ministry of Education has decided to compile a relatively comprehensive publication entitled "The Current Status of Chinese Education." The content is divided into higher education (including trends of overseas students and universities, and the current status of departments), general education (including the current status of primary and secondary schools, normal schools, and vocational schools), social education, Mongolian and Tibetan education, etc. The heads of departments, section chiefs, secretaries, and counselors are responsible for writing the articles, which are expected to be completed and compiled by January next year.

Anhui Provincial Education Conference Concludes 204

Anhui News. The Anhui Provincial Local Education Reorganization Conference continued its fifth general meeting on the morning of the 25th to conclude the motions of various groups. In the afternoon, a closing ceremony was held and the conference declaration was passed. The situation on the morning and afternoon of that day is recorded below. The fifth general meeting was held at 8:30 AM on the 25th at the old site of the Education Department, with 91 attendees, 10 observers, and 2 audience members. Yang Lian chaired the meeting. After the chairman reported on various matters, discussion began. The Education Affairs Group reviewed the report. The first motion was to request the Education Department to formulate a plan for the province to implement compulsory education. It was a merger of 18 motions. The review opinion was that the formulation of the plan must be based on the following principles: 1. The total mobilization of elementary school students in the province to be "little teachers". 2. The total mobilization of literate adults in the province to be "transmission teachers". 3. The total mobilization of intellectuals in the province to guide and promote modern education. 4. The elementary schools in the province must be reformed. 5. The private schools in the province must be reformed. 6. The normal schools in the province must be reformed. 7. Materials and tools should be supplied or reformed. The formulation of the plan should pay attention to the following compulsory and assessment principles: 1. Stipulate the procedure for popularization. 2. Compulsory methods. 3. Request the Legislative Yuan to formulate a crime of obstructing progress. 4. Should stipulate assessment methods for local administrative officials, education administrative personnel, and schools at all levels to promote universal education. The Education Department should organize a compulsory education research institute to plan and implement universal education. Request the provincial government to issue an order on New Year's Day of the 24th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1935] to announce that compulsory education will be implemented throughout the province within a specified time limit. Resolution: Approved according to the review opinion. The second motion was to propose the organization of a Rural Construction Research Institute. Resolution: Approved according to the review opinion. The third motion was to propose the establishment of a Rural Service Personnel Training Class. A merger of three motions. Resolution: The Education Department should refer to the various proposals and formulate an implementation plan. The fourth motion was that all elementary schools in the province should accept the "little teacher" system. Resolution: Approved. The Education Administration Affairs and Education Affairs groups jointly reviewed the report. The first motion was to implement the integration of political education, culture, health, and sanitation to improve education efficiency and promote rural revival. Resolution: Approved according to the review opinion. The Education Affairs Group reviewed the report. The fifth motion was to improve private schools in the province. A merger of nine motions. Resolution: Revised and approved. The sixth motion was to promote social education. Resolution: Please refer to the Department's selection for use. The seventh motion was that a primary vocational school should be established in each administrative district. Resolution: Please refer to the Department's selection. The eighth motion was to stipulate the number of teachers allocated to rural elementary schools and the number of students in each class. Resolution: Please refer to the Department's selection for implementation. The ninth motion was to abolish the weekly holiday. Resolution: Schools can consider the situation and handle it automatically. There is no need to request an explicit order to abolish it. The Education Funding Group reported. The first motion was to maintain the additional tax on mineral education. Resolution: It should continue to be collected to prioritize education funds. The second motion was to provide relief to disaster-stricken areas for education. A merger of two motions. Resolution: Request the provincial government to allocate 500,000 yuan or issue public bonds, and allocate official wasteland as school land to increase income. The third motion was to use temple property without monks as education expenses, and the fourth motion was that an additional education fee should be added to property transfers. It was resolved that Motion C should be retained, and that Motion D should be decided by the county. The fourth motion was that county education expenses should be accumulated in an education fund every year to prepare for disasters. Resolution: The Department should formulate a plan. The fifth motion was to request the provincial government to issue a notice to all counties that school property should be exempt from various miscellaneous donations and miscellaneous labor services. Resolution: Approved. The sixth motion was that secondary education in each county should be subsidized by the Department as much as possible. Resolution: Please refer to the Department's selection for implementation. The seventh motion was that the central or provincial government should be responsible for county education expenses to provide subsidies. A merger of two motions. Resolution: Please refer to the Department's review. The eighth motion was that the provincial government should be requested to raise funds to repay the unpaid education expenses from before the 16th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1927]. Resolution: The conference should submit a request to the provincial government to order the finance department to allocate funds for repayment. The ninth motion was to use abandoned public houses and temples that should not be worshiped as elementary school buildings. A merger of three motions. Resolution: Approved. The tenth motion was that newly established counties should be given discretionary assistance from the provincial treasury for education expenses. A merger of two motions. Resolution: It should be forwarded to the provincial government for review. The Education Guidance Group reviewed the report. The first motion was to effectively promote the Provincial People's Education Center's guidance of county people's education. Resolution: Please refer to the Department's selection for implementation. The second motion was to improve the school inspector's exchange inspection method. Resolution: Approved. The third motion was that district education committee members should be transferred by the Education Bureau for exchange inspection. Resolution: Retained. The fourth motion was that primary education instructors should be added to provincial affiliated elementary schools. Resolution: Retained. The fifth motion was that elementary school teachers should guide private schools nearby. Resolution: Forwarded to the Department for reference. The sixth motion was how to stipulate various levels of guidance systems. A merger of two motions. Resolution: Please stipulate by the Department. The seventh motion was how to issue guidance publications. A merger of four motions. Resolution: Recommended to the Education Department. The eighth motion was how normal schools should guide local education. Resolution: Approved. The Education Affairs Group reported the first motion that each county should establish a science laboratory. A merger of two motions. Resolution: Approved. The ninth motion was to request the provincial government to allocate funds for education in bandit areas. Resolution: Sent to the Special Education Office for reference. Temporary motions: Negotiate with the central government to offset the education expense losses after the abolition of harsh miscellaneous taxes. Huang Daolin and more than ten others were designated as negotiators. A proposal organization committee was formed, and Zhou Huazhen and others were designated to organize. Please have the Education Department inform the Rural Cooperation Committee to cooperate with elementary schools throughout the province as much as possible. Two motions were also passed to request the Department to inform the Construction Department to order provincial farms to select pig and chicken breeds as much as possible and to establish veterinary hospitals to improve rural production. The meeting adjourned.

The closing ceremony was held at 3:00 PM and the declaration was passed. Members were scheduled to visit various educational institutions in the provincial capital in groups starting on the 26th. Chairman Ma Dai held individual talks with members starting on the afternoon of the 26th. Tao Xingzhi stayed here to complete his proposed compulsory education plan and did not leave. He returned to Shanghai on the 27th.

Recent News from the Daxia People's Education Experiment Zone 214

The People's Education Experiment Zone attached to Daxia University has added a Rural Experimental Primary School and a Workers' School this semester. Work in all areas is becoming increasingly intense. For example, the Xujiazhai People's Education Center, in addition to the library, exhibition room, and public tea garden, is also implementing mobile teaching and experimenting with a mother-child mutual teaching system. The Jijiaku Village Nianer Cooperative organizes textile, laundry, and handicraft cooperative groups, focusing on economic activities to implement livelihood-based education. The Zhoujiaqiao Workers' School is striving to improve the lives of workers, guiding students to organize student associations, operate consumer cooperatives, and build roads. The Meiyuan Rural Experimental Primary School held a villager's get-together last week, with forty to fifty students and parents attending, creating a very joyful atmosphere. Mr. Zhou Dagang, a teacher at the school, raised the issue of cooperation in education between the school and the family, and Mr. Jiang Dixian gave a lecture on methods of agricultural improvement. The villagers were very understanding and happy to receive guidance. The Gui Lane Cooperative Education Society recently organized a sales cooperative, which has been established. It obtained a vegetable stall license from the public concession racetrack vegetable market, which the villagers were very happy about. Currently, the vegetables produced in the village are all sold by the cooperative, saving 8% in commissions, which is of great benefit to the farmers' economy. Furthermore, the villagers, recognizing that the village road from the village to Zhongshan Road varies in width and height, making it inconvenient to transport agricultural products, held a villager's meeting and decided to use the winter to build a cooperative road. Construction began on the 25th of this month and is expected to be completed soon. The road is 16 feet wide and three miles long, and is one of the two major arteries of the area. Once completed, the area's transportation network can be said to be complete. In addition, to promote the national calendar and revitalize the spirit of the people, the area held a New Life Movement on New Year's Day, followed by a funfair at 4 p.m. All the villagers of the area participated and paraded through the entire area, which is bound to be a grand occasion.

Tao Xingzhi Speaks on Popular Education in Greater Shanghai 215

Education expert Mr. Tao Xingzhi invented the "Little Teacher System" to implement a popular education movement. He has already run Hai Gong and Hai Tuan experiments with remarkable results. Yesterday morning, Director Pan of this city, at the Chen Yingshi Memorial Hall in Lake Society, with over six hundred people in attendance, specially invited Mr. Tao to give a public lecture as a model for this city. Mr. Tao cited the Little Teacher System as a method for popular education in poor countries, and proved that the power of children is great, truly being the vanguard of popular education. Mr. Tao said that the Little Teacher System can break through the twelve difficulties of popular education, especially the Huajiao People's Basic School, organized by Mr. Huang Jingwan, which is the first Little Teacher experimental site in this city. Moreover, the Little Teachers can popularize life education and cultivate national vitality. With this, Shanghai's illiteracy can be eliminated in no more than three years. Director Pan expressed deep sincerity towards the Little Teachers, and encouraged over a hundred teachers from public and private schools to make a firm resolution to implement the Little Teacher System. Mr. Tao's speech was interspersed with humor, lasting for about three hours, and the listeners were all moved. At the end, the Commercial Press gave each person a calendar diary as a souvenir.

Gains and Losses of China's Medical Education in the Past, Present, and Future (Continued) 228

— Lecture by Wang Qizhang, Notes by Chen Sheng Bai and Jiang Huiming

Current Chinese Medical Education

In today's society, are there people who understand clearly and study foreign knowledge? Probably seven or eight out of ten still adhere to the existing traditional Chinese medicine, thinking there is no need to learn foreign medicine. It is truly not easy to find someone who is truly determined to use foreign scientific medicine to assimilate China's inherent medicine. Therefore, to this day, approximately two-thirds of the scientific medical education institutions were founded by foreigners or are subsidized by foreign forces. This kind of non-automatic, unconscious cultural import is simply an invaded colonial education - alienated education; rather than an automatic, autonomous national education - assimilated education.

Look at the United States in the Philippines; everything is Americanized. On the surface, the Philippines will become the second America and become a great and strong country in the world. Unfortunately, the American education received by the Philippines is enslaving education, colonial education, and has only formed a base for the United States in East Asia! Similarly, Annam is Frenchified, and Taiwan and Korea are Japanized. We know that if you want people to educate you, if you want people to help you, people are willing to sacrifice; as long as the person willing to sacrifice is not a fool, I dare say that those people must have intentions, either to fight for power or to seek profit. There is definitely no true sacrifice without a second thought. Perhaps I am saying this too aggressively.

There are many such examples, such as the schools in the Shanghai concessions. The talents they have cultivated cannot be said to be few; however, they are of no benefit to China, and even harmful. The people who come from there cannot do business for China, they can only be compradors for foreign firms, clerks in offices, translators in patrol rooms, and do work of assisting the wicked. We see foreigners taking Chinese money to educate Chinese children. Can we say that they are unwilling to sacrifice? In fact, their intentions are for themselves, not for us Chinese. Therefore, all Chinese people should know that this is not educating citizens for China, but rather providing many citizens to others. Some people say: academics are academics, politics are politics, this is fundamentally wrong. However, there are direct and indirect relationships between academics and politics, but academics and politics cannot be separated. For example, a scientist invents something. Of course, this is a so-called academic contribution, but after his invention, it gives the country tremendous help in terms of economy and politics. Look: the progress of chemistry will lead to the occurrence of chemical warfare; the progress of machinery will lead to the appearance of tanks and mortars. If this kind of weapon is used for me, it can protect the country. If used for others, it can destroy the country. A moment's reflection will make it clear: people educate you, sacrifice for you, spend effort for you, and spend money for you, just to cultivate a group of willing dogs. Will this group of dogs understand national principles? Will they understand their position clearly? What is the background of the great and solemn League of Nations? What is its role? A discerning person can of course see through its dark secrets. So I think that the medical education in China today still relies on the education of others. It is still tending towards alienation, and the future is very dangerous. For example, those who like England and the United States are single-mindedly trying to turn China into England and the United States, those who like France are trying to turn China into France, and perhaps those who like Germany and Japan are trying to turn China into Germany and Japan... If one day their respective desires are satisfied, China will no longer be China, but will have become a foreign China.

V. Future of Medical Education in China

Since we feel that our level is not enough, and at the same time we feel that simply imitating others is not thorough enough, then how should we deal with the medical education problem in the future? Because our knowledge is immature, of course we cannot but learn their foreign knowledge. If we cannot recognize their characters, then we cannot understand the content of their scholarship. We must recognize clearly that we may as well learn their characters and scholarship, but we want to use it to assimilate, not to alienate. Even if we see that foreign things are better than ours, we like them, admire them, and learn them, and abandon the things that we don't like, all are possible; but we must recognize clearly that we want to learn from it, not just become it. If we also become it, and are alienated by them, then it will be terrible!

(A) Importance of National Education We need to further discuss here how we can avoid alienation?

I think the most important thing is to lay the foundation for national education. If there is no foundation for national education, then you cannot learn foreign scholarship or use foreign things. Because with a foundation of national education, you can avoid foreignization, you can use foreign things to assimilate, you can take foreign scholarship for your own use, and make the country receive great benefits, and even be able to surpass foreign things and promote the national quintessence. Therefore, even if you enter a foreign school and receive foreign education, you will not be foreignized. If a person does not have a good foundation in national education, no matter how studious or intelligent he is, the result is that although his appearance, name, and nationality are Chinese, he is actually foreignized, he is already a foreigner.

Educators have said: "General education is national education, national education has a foundation, and then there is academic education. If there is no national education, there is no academic education."

In the past, there were countless Chinese students studying abroad. The result is that they can only speak a few foreign languages, wear a few foreign suits, use foreign things, be driven by foreigners, and increase economic and political aggression and power for foreign countries. These bad phenomena are all because they have not received good autonomous national education. This is a huge crisis in the future of Chinese academic education!

Therefore, I personally advocate that if Chinese national education has a foundation, then the future of Chinese medical education has hope, and Chinese medical education will be effective; otherwise, Chinese medical education will only get worse and worse, and the future of Chinese medical education is simply unimaginable.

In order to see this clearly, if we follow the current educational policy, I think the Chinese government simply does not need to send students abroad to be foreignized and become foreign teachers for Chinese people; it is better to hire foreigners straightforwardly to teach in China, which can save a lot of trouble and be more effective, right?

(B) Stages for Learning Foreign Culture We can divide learning foreign culture into three stages:

The first stage - learning its appearance, not learning its essence. For example, wearing a Western suit, we can only learn its appearance. The raw materials for the Western suit must still be domestic products, but not foreign products to be alienated by it; if you wear Chinese clothes and use foreign raw materials, the result is also equivalent to alienation. Therefore, when we bring foreign things into China, we only need to take its characters as symbols, not use foreign characters to represent Chinese characters, and treat foreign texts as

Public Health Assistant and the Needs of Society 229

— Yang Renyuan

The rural hygiene work of Takahashi's Hygiene Office (formerly known as the Takahashi Rural Hygiene Model Area) occupies a considerable position in China's current health undertakings, and there is no need to introduce it further.

At the end of last year, the director of the office, Zhang Wei, and the hosts, Dr. Zhu Bangren and Dr. Lai Douyan, in response to the need to popularize health education among the people and the fact that bankrupt farmers cannot afford doctors, took advantage of their ability to learn while doing, and requested the municipal health bureau to approve the establishment of a public health assistant training class. In this day and age, where poverty and disease are rampant and scientific doctors are scarce, the establishment of such training classes in rural areas is necessary for social reform and the future of the nation, and should be vigorously promoted. The following is a miscellaneous record for the reference of those who study China's health undertakings.

This training class is neither the same as the ordinary assistants who change medicine in the outpatient department, nor like a second-rate nurse. The purpose of the training is to have them go to the countryside where people cannot afford doctors and do not necessarily need doctors, to do preventive work, school hygiene, family visits, and health education, so it is called a public health assistant training class.

They were afraid of recruiting the type of young masters and young ladies, whose training would be useless, so the first thing they paid attention to when recruiting was to have a hard-working spirit, preferably young people who grew up in the countryside, because only those who grew up in the countryside know the situation and suffering of the countryside, and will be willing to go back to their hometowns and work hard.

The general situation of the recruitment is that those with junior high school education or equivalent qualifications can enroll. The term is one year, with the first half year being the training period and the second half year being the internship period. During the training period, living expenses are subsidized. If it is sent by an organization, the subsidy is provided by the organization. Because it was the first trial, the recruitment was limited to eight people. Later, many people requested to join, so three more people were added, making a total of eleven, and classes started on January 1st of this year.

The teaching method is to learn and then do, and to seek further practical knowledge from doing things. For example, if you have school hygiene in the morning, you will go to the school in the afternoon to help with physical examinations and train students, and bring back any problems to solve.

The subjects taught are anatomy, physiology, pathology, bacteriology, disinfection, infectious diseases, first aid, pharmacology, disease prevention, bandaging, school hygiene, environmental hygiene, factory hygiene, maternal and child hygiene, social investigation, statistics, nursing, family visits, and applied writing (including ethics, sociology, English, Chinese, and other subjects), teaching them roughly according to the needs of the situation. Because they do not want to treat diseases, they do not teach the subjects related to treatment, except for first aid and the application of ordinary medicines. The rest of the time is spent on field work and discussing problems.

The first half of the year's classes ended at the end of June, and from July 1st, they were assigned to various rural areas for internships according to their interests and strengths, and in this short period of time, they have already achieved considerable results.

If we calmly study it, in this situation where public health is extremely underdeveloped, scientific doctors are scarce and most of them are unwilling to go to the countryside, and farmers cannot find doctors to treat their illnesses, this kind of talent can indeed prevent diseases, reduce the suffering of the villagers, and remedy this transitional period in China. On the other hand, they can also be pioneers in popularizing health education and making people believe in scientific medicine. I think it is very suitable for the needs of the current society.

In recent years, the standard of living in society has increased several times, and industry has been affected by the bankruptcy of rural areas. Not only is there no surplus, but there is also a deficit, so the regular expenses originally subsidized to our school have to be discounted and paid. The school can only maintain the status quo with difficulty.

That is what is considered assimilation; otherwise, if we learn from foreigners, we ourselves will also become foreigners. Such alienation is very dangerous.
