6 Conclusion

China's medical education: In the past || Not worth mentioning! Now || Very dangerous!

In the future || We must recognize the background and role of foreigners, determine our own views, determine the goals of learning foreign culture, and absorb the essence of foreign countries to make it Chinese, not worship foreign culture and become foreignized.

Foreign languages can only be regarded as a sign for learning foreign culture and are not fundamentally related to the future of the entire education. For the sake of the vital issue of Chinese education, especially the future of medical education, we should still focus on the needs of national education. || End ||

It is difficult, how can we talk about expanding equipment? Therefore, the collection of specimens depends entirely on the self-efforts of our students. Medicine attaches great importance to practice, such as anatomy in basic courses. It is not enough to just read books and memorize terms to understand it. We must carry out dissection and see the actual situation to clarify the truth. Nantong was originally a prefecture and county. In the past, there were many executions of robbers and criminals. According to the government's order, the bodies of those without family members could be issued to local medical institutions for dissection and practice. However, the people of Tongdi were not enlightened (perhaps the entire China is like this). In the past, after our hospital received the bodies and carried out dissection, the Tongxian government was criticized. Therefore, in recent years, every time the corpses were executed, even if there were no family members, after repeated contacts with our hospital, the responsible authorities always used clever words to shirk their responsibility. For this reason, what our students rely on as anatomical specimens is only the exposed bones in the desolate tombs and wild graves.

A week ago, students from our hospital picked up bone specimens on the barren tombs of the Animal Husbandry Farm of our school's Agricultural College, but they were not understood by the villagers, who reported to the public security organs. The public security organs also implemented detention and sent them to the court for handling. Fortunately, the court was able to understand the pure purpose of scientific research and gave a lenient treatment. Unexpectedly, not only did the society not explain the misunderstanding, but some fabricated facts, and some made unwarranted criticisms. For the sake of the future of medicine and the happiness of mankind, we cannot but feel deeply pained, and we cannot but make some statements.

Medicine is for treating diseases and saving people. If you want to treat diseases, you should first have an accurate diagnosis. Acupuncture and medicine are secondary. Whether it is diagnosis or treatment, it will not be effective if you do not first understand the structure of our body and its physiological and pathological conditions. Physiological anatomy is to understand the position of the anatomical organs and their organizational structure. Pathological anatomy is to observe the causes of diseases and their changes. Bones are the foundation of physiological anatomy. First, know the structure of the bones, then know the position of the organs, the attachment of muscles and ligaments, and the passage of blood vessels and nerves. From this, further study the mysteries of physiology and pathology, examine the causes of diseases, and treat them. Then it will be easier to see results, just like an engineer with a machine. If you don't first understand the structure of the machine, how can you know the movement and damage of the machine, let alone repair and improve it? This is why Western medicine is called scientific medicine, and it is also the key to the rapid progress of European and American medicine, which our country cannot match.

People often hope that doctors can make accurate diagnoses and reasonable treatments, but they do not understand the doctor's dissection of corpses and collection of bones. How contradictory is this? This is worth noting.

From a philosophical point of view, "death" is the final destination of life. After death, everything cannot be missed, nor does it need to be missed. What about the body? What's the difference between cremation, water burial, bird burial, animal burial, and thick coffins, beautiful clothes, and decorated graves for the dead? It's just to comfort the living. This is worth noting.

I heard that returning birds have the saying that instead of rotting with grass and trees, why not contribute their bodies for the research of the medical community, turn uselessness into usefulness, and seek the development of medicine and the happiness of the people? This is worth noting.

Even if we take a step back and talk about the facts, the barren tomb belongs to the Animal Husbandry Farm of our school's Agricultural College. It lacks family members and is unattended. Usually, white bones are everywhere and trampled by livestock. Why is it inappropriate for us to collect them as specimens? Clever words of charity are even more slippery. This is worth noting.

In short, in this incident, the so-called principal offender (actually, it cannot be called a crime) is worthy of admiration for his spirit of scientific loyalty, and his actions are not inappropriate in any way. The villagers are misled by traditional concepts and superstitious myths and heresies, which is understandable. However, it is really incomprehensible and deeply regrettable that people in the society fabricate their words and criticize them.

In Western countries, the dissection of corpses and the collection of bones have long been commonplace. It is appropriate that their medicine is thriving and making great progress, which our country cannot hope to match.

Since thousands of years ago, China's patriarchal concept has been deeply rooted. Wearing mourning clothes and thick coffins are regarded as major events in human relations. Destroying corpses and harming bodies are regarded as rebellious acts. After a long period of accumulation, it is not easy to reform. However, for the sake of the future of medicine and the happiness of mankind, the author dares to put forward the following suggestions to seek the correction and adoption of people in the society.

(1) The government authorities should quickly formulate and implement concrete regulations to protect and encourage the research on corpse dissection.

(2) The media should always discuss the value of medical dissection from a fair standpoint and correct the corrupt and erroneous views of the public.

(3) Intellectuals should set an example, embrace the spirit of fearlessness, and contribute the corpses of individuals or family members for medical dissection to promote it.

(4) The medical community should unite and strive to urge the government to help the media eliminate the erroneous views of the public, and especially respect the dissected corpses and conduct detailed research to meet the actual situation.

If the above-mentioned points can be fulfilled, fulfilled their responsibilities, and implemented in a practical way, then the accumulated habits can be eliminated, and the future of medicine and the happiness of the people can be truly relied on.

Common Sense Questions and Answers on Diseases 231

— Cheng Hanzhang

(49) Intestinal Obstruction (Continued)

(Q) In addition to the symptoms mentioned above, what other symptoms are there in strangulated intestinal obstruction?

(A) In addition to eroding the intestinal wall, bacteria can also invade the mesentery. The onset of the disease is mostly sudden, with symptoms of concussion. The pain is very severe, and the entire abdomen is felt. Vomiting is also very severe, occurring one or twenty times a day, mixed with bile, but with little fecal odor and color. The abdominal wall is very tense, but the degree of bloating is slight; and there is local resistance, tenderness, and bulging.

(Q) What are the symptoms of paralytic intestinal obstruction?

(A) The symptoms are the same as those of obturator intestinal obstruction. The bloating is limited. The pain is caused by the underlying disease. Vomiting is delayed. There is no noise in the intestines.

(Q) What are the symptoms of spastic intestinal obstruction?

(A) Although it is also similar to obturator intestinal obstruction, there is no vomiting of feces or concussion, the pain is also mild, and the overall condition is relatively good.

(Q) What is the treatment for intestinal obstruction?

(A) Different treatments should be given depending on the condition.

(Q) How should attention be paid to the patient's diet?

(A) For acute obstruction, fasting should be done. For subacute obstruction, a small amount of food that will not accumulate in the intestines, such as milk and milk powder, can be eaten. For chronic stenosis, a small amount of nutritious food without residue can be eaten.

(Q) What kinds of food should be avoided?

(A) The foods and medicines that must be avoided are those that easily cause constipation, such as strong tea, gelatinous food, foods containing lime, and bismuth preparations. There are also foods and drinks that produce gas, such as carbonated drinks and potatoes.

(Q) How should abdominal pain and tension be treated?

(A) A warm compress can be applied to the abdomen.

(Q) What should be done if the patient is very thirsty?

(A) Ice cubes can be held in the mouth, or warm tea can be used to rinse the mouth. Saltwater injection is also effective.

(Q) Can opium be used when there is intestinal peristalsis with pain and vomiting?

(A) It can be used, but it is absolutely forbidden in paralytic intestinal obstruction.

(Q) Is gastric lavage effective?

(A) Gastric lavage is very effective. This can not only reduce the contents that are regurgitated in the intestines, but also eliminate the phenomenon of autointoxication.

(Q) How is electrical therapy performed for this disease?

(A) First, inject 100 cc of physiological saline into the intestines, insert a zhengchang conductor (cathode), and apply zheng stream electricity for 15 minutes (10 to 15 milliamperes). It is most suitable for paralytic abdominal obstruction.

(Q) When is surgical operation necessary?

(A) If treatment is ineffective within 24 hours of the onset of the disease, only surgical laparotomy can be performed. This is especially true for strangulated intestinal obstruction. The earlier the laparotomy, the better. (End)

A Brief Introduction to Pulmonary Tuberculosis 232

— Hu Jiayan

(5) Specialized Diagnosis || Tuberculin Reaction

The diagnosis of pulmonary tuberculosis is most accurate and reliable when tubercle bacilli are found in the sputum. This situation has already been discussed above! However, this proof is not easy for every patient to obtain. Even important clinical symptoms such as hemoptysis, cough, increased temperature, and weight loss are sometimes completely lacking, but the result will also determine that he is suffering from this disease. This aspect of the harvest is in addition to the various examinations mentioned above, there is another specialized diagnostic method; this is the tuberculin described now!

What is "tuberculin"? It is made by refining tubercle bacilli and was first invented by the pioneer of bacteriology, Master Koch; hence, it also has the name "tuberculin". Its application in the treatment of this disease is very broad, and there are considerable achievements that can be secretly observed; the details of this will be described in a separate chapter later. In addition, in terms of diagnosis, when the disease starts in the early stage, the clinical symptoms are not obvious, and whether the doctor's decision is correct or not is in doubt. But if the patient is found to have a positive tuberculin reaction, this problem will be solved almost immediately! With a clear understanding of the disease, it is of course possible to start with the right treatment plan as soon as possible! This is a win-win situation, and I don't think anyone will deny the convenience it gives to both the patient and the doctor.

What is the tuberculin reaction like? It is divided into three aspects: local lesions and the whole body. The local reaction refers to the place where tuberculin is inoculated or injected, and swelling and pain will mostly occur. The reaction of the lesion refers to the increase of redness and swelling in the lesion and the presentation of an inflammatory reaction. This is a very obvious example in lupus vulgaris, which is a skin tuberculosis; of course, it cannot be seen in pulmonary tuberculosis. However, clinically, there are also symptoms such as increased cough, increased sputum volume, and increased muddy vesicular sounds. Among the systemic reactions, the most significant proof is the rise in body temperature. Just a rise of half a degree Celsius higher than usual can be regarded as a positive reaction. This rise will usually occur six or eight hours after the injection, reaching its peak after 24 hours (up to 39 or 40 degrees Celsius), and then gradually decrease over two or three days until it returns to the pre-injection state. In addition to the rise in body temperature, symptoms such as headache, restlessness, nausea, and vomiting will mostly occur at the same time. || The discovery of these three positive reactions is usually between seven or eight hours and as late as ten to twelve hours; if it occurs after a few days, we can simply say that it is not related to tuberculin inoculation or injection.

Common Sense of Hygiene for Ears, Nose, Throat, and Eyes 233

— Tang Renjin

(29) Real Fuli (commonly known as Diphtheria) (Continued)

▲ Prevention of Real Fuli

Since Real Fuli is recognized as an infectious disease caused by Real Fuli bacilli, it must of course follow the general regulations for infectious diseases. Send it to an infectious disease hospital immediately for isolation. However, in fact, it is not always possible. Because sometimes parents are unwilling to send their sick children to the hospital for isolation and treatment, so most of them are isolated at home and seek medical treatment. At this time, it is absolutely impossible to share food and accommodation with the patient, especially for children. The bedroom must always be kept ventilated, and it is better to have direct sunlight exposure. All utensils, toys, and bedrooms should be carefully disinfected with disinfectant solution. It is better to use steam disinfection. Furthermore, oral hygiene is also important. Use sterilized water to rinse your mouth frequently. As for the injection of preventive serum, it must be injected after a doctor's examination. However, because its defensive power disappears after a certain period, most people are often unwilling to inject it.

▲ Treatment of Real Fuli

The only effective treatment for Real Fuli is to inject Real Fuli serum. Whether it is pharyngeal Real Fuli, laryngeal Real Fuli, or nasal Real Fuli, if a definite diagnosis is obtained, Real Fuli serum should be injected immediately. The earlier the injection, the faster the effect. The amount of serum is calculated in units. The number of units depends on the date of onset, the severity of the disease, the age of the patient, and the constitution. Usually, the serum injection unit for laryngeal Real Fuli is always above 10,000. According to our doctors' experience, it is better to err on the side of injecting too many units than too few. Regarding this point, the attending physician can of course consider the situation and inject it as much as possible. You can rest assured. When serum is injected, and later after it is injected, two diseases often occur. These diseases do not necessarily occur with every injection. Now I will briefly describe the phenomena of these two diseases as follows.

(1) Allergy. In people who have been injected with serum a week ago, if a second serum injection is given, there are often severe and terrifying reactions, sometimes even endangering life. (Even if the first serum injection was many years ago, this is still the case.) Fortunately, it is still relatively easy to prevent this terrible allergy. That is, when injecting, a very small amount should be injected first. After half an hour or an hour, if there is no reaction, inject a slightly larger amount, and after another half an hour or an hour, the full amount can be injected. The reason for injecting in stages is because it can preemptively numb the patient's sensitivity. This injection in stages can probably avoid encountering the above-mentioned danger. Now, experienced doctors generally ask if they have been injected with serum before when injecting various serums, or directly implement injections in stages. They are simply trying to prevent this allergy in advance.

(2) Serum sickness. This serum sickness is not specifically found in Real Fuli serum. Other serums can also occur. Its symptoms are that about a week after the serum injection, red, finger-sized, urticaria-like spots often appear from the face, trunk, to the limbs. The itching is severe, which is quite painful. At the same time, the temperature also rises, which often causes fear among patients and their families. In fact, I dare to guarantee that it is harmless, and even more that there is no danger to life. Generally, after three or four days, or up to a week, the fever will drop and the rash will subside, and health will be restored. If laxatives and calcium agents are given, then its recovery date will be even faster.

Furthermore, if laryngeal Real Fuli has fallen into a state of suffocation and there is no time to inject serum, or if serum has been injected but breathing difficulties become more severe, a tracheotomy should be performed immediately to open another airway. Seek urgent breathing to save the day. Often, the suffocating, purplish-blue complexion can be changed to a ruddy color by several smooth breaths, and the dying life can be saved. It is a pity that most families are unwilling to have their children undergo this operation, which is really a pity (End)

A General Description of Malaria (3) 234

— Wang Xiaolan

▲Malaria Symptoms▼

(1) Tertian and Quartan Malaria: In malaria sufferers, the time from the introduction of malaria parasites into the blood to the onset of the disease is called the incubation period. It is approximately ten to fourteen days for tertian malaria and twelve to twenty-one days for quartan malaria. The tertian malaria parasite matures in forty-eight hours, hence the disease occurs every other day. Repeated infections can cause alternating day fevers, resembling daily malaria. The quartan malaria parasite matures in seventy-two hours, causing fever every three days, commonly known as "fever on both ends of the fourth day." When the fever occurs for two consecutive days with a one-day interval, it is called "repeated quartan malaria." If the fever occurs daily, it is called "triple quartan malaria." If several types of malaria parasites are mixed or repeatedly infected, the chills and fever will occur irregularly, making it difficult to distinguish without blood tests. Although tertian and quartan malaria are mild forms of the disease, if left untreated, they can develop into chronic malaria or induce heart and lung diseases.

During a malaria attack, the body temperature rises sharply, reaching around 40 degrees Celsius. Peripheral blood vessels constrict, reducing blood flow, causing chills and shivering, goosebumps, and chattering teeth. The skin becomes pale and cold, and the lips and fingertips turn blue. This phase lasts an average of one to two hours. Subsequently, as the fever reaches its peak, blood flows to the peripheral blood vessels, causing the skin to become hot and flushed, with a red face and thirst. The spleen becomes congested and enlarged. Auscultation of the heart reveals systolic murmurs associated with the fever. This phase lasts an average of three to four hours. Finally, the body temperature drops, and peripheral blood vessels dilate, causing profuse sweating all over the body. Urine output gradually increases, the spleen shrinks, and the symptoms subside. This phase lasts an average of two to three hours, gradually returning to normal. When the malaria parasites mature and divide again, releasing merozoites into the blood, another attack occurs. However, the timing of the attacks may vary slightly, hence the terms "progressive" or "retrogressive."

In addition to chills and fever, the number of red blood cells and hemoglobin in the blood decreases, leading to anemia. Blood tests can reveal basophilic stippling in red blood cells, as well as an increase in transitional and large mononuclear leukocytes. Patients often experience pain in all bones and joints, or develop creeping eruptions and rose spots. Inflammation of the respiratory tract can cause coughing. During the chill phase, the skin is dry and sensation is dulled, with a rapid and weak pulse and rapid breathing. During the fever and sweating phase, the skin is flushed and sensation is hypersensitive, with a full and rapid pulse. Intermittent pulsus bigeminus may also occur. Neurological symptoms often include headache, neuralgia, convulsions, paralysis, drowsiness, and altered movements. Digestive symptoms often include stomach pain, jaundice, nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, belching, and loss of appetite. During the intervals between attacks, the urine often contains urobilin.

(2) Pernicious Malaria: Pernicious malaria is more severe and often leads to severe anemia and malarial cachexia. It occurs more frequently in tropical regions, with an incubation period of approximately five to ten days. After the initial attack, basophilic stippling can be detected in red blood cells. The maturation of the malaria parasites is irregular, causing erratic fevers that may occur daily, every other day, or several times a day. There may be repeated chills and fevers, or no chills and no sweating. The fever may persist for a long time. As such, there are terms like "tropical daily fever," "midday malaria," and "summer-autumn fever." Because it often presents with symptoms like lethargy, drowsiness, delirium, mania, convulsions, paralysis, vomiting and diarrhea, cold extremities, jaundice, stomach pain, low blood pressure, collapse, loss of consciousness, and hematuria, it is further classified into somnolent, delirious, choleraic, icteric, gastralgic, algid, syncopal, and hematuric types of pernicious malaria.

(3) Masked Malaria, Chronic Malaria, and Malarial Cachexia: Masked malaria presents with mild or no fever. Patients often experience periodic neuralgia in the trigeminal, occipital, intercostal, lumbar, abdominal, and internal organs. The spleen is enlarged, and patients may occasionally experience hemiplegia, loss of consciousness, convulsions, edema, rash, dizziness, respiratory inflammation, and gastroenteritis. Chronic malaria often develops from pernicious malaria or from inadequate treatment of tertian or quartan malaria. The fever is mild and irregular, with a yellowish-gray skin, anemia, shortness of breath, and enlarged spleen and liver. Patients may occasionally experience gastroenteritis, respiratory inflammation, kidney inflammation, and arteriosclerosis. Malarial cachexia is even more dangerous and often occurs after pernicious or chronic malaria. The face appears ashen, and the extremities or the entire body may be edematous. The skin and mucous membranes are prone to bleeding. Jaundice, ascites, and symptoms involving the nervous, circulatory, respiratory, and digestive systems often occur successively, leading to debilitation and death.

(4) Blackwater Fever: Blackwater fever is an atypical form of malaria caused by the rapid destruction of a large number of red blood cells. It is often triggered by quinine treatment for malaria. It is more common in tropical regions, but also occurs sporadically in Yunnan, Guangdong, and Fujian provinces in China. It usually occurs within a few hours after taking quinine, with sudden chills, shivering, headache, back pain, nausea, vomiting, and a rapid rise in body temperature to over 40 degrees Celsius. Jaundice, hematuria, bloody stools, subcutaneous hemorrhage, and enlargement of the liver and spleen may also occur. The urine is dark brown like soy sauce, with a specific gravity of 1.030 to 1.035, and contains large amounts of protein, renal epithelial cells, and hemoglobin. Severe cases may present with impaired consciousness and difficulty breathing, and death may occur during the acute phase due to heart failure. In mild cases, the symptoms may subside within a few hours after the attack, but repeated attacks are still dangerous. (To be continued)

Page 17

Free Talk

Ideal and Reality 235

— Ren Baige

I once saw somewhere the following words: "Marriage is a besieged city; those on the outside want to rush in and take a look, while those inside want to escape." In the past, I found these words interesting. Now, after hearing the long sighs and short breaths of many married friends, I find them even more worthy of contemplation.

Life is truly like a journey to visit scenic spots. Before reaching a certain destination, the heart is always filled with endless longing and desire. Once a destination is reached, only a sense of emptiness and indifference remains. Marriage, this besieged city, is merely a famous city that is difficult to visit multiple times on a full-length journey. We can very well extend these words to all stages of life and contemplate them! Many people would think this way.

This way of thinking is very common. Haven't many equally thought-provoking sayings already been popular among our common people? For example, sayings like "the other mountain looks taller" and "distant spring water is clear, nearby spring water is muddy" are of this kind. In elegant circles, our gentlemen and ladies also use a fashionable way of expressing this: ideals are beautiful, reality is ugly, or at least reality is never as beautiful as ideals. Therefore, people pursue ideals and are dissatisfied with reality, constantly running in and out between ideals and reality.

In a truly ugly real society, it is perfectly acceptable to say that reality is never as beautiful as ideals; it is also acceptable to say that people pursue ideals and are dissatisfied with reality, but these words should not be absolutized and eternalized. Our gentlemen and ladies often like to absolutize and eternalize all concepts. According to their logic, these words can be simply stated as follows: reality is never as beautiful as ideals, and all ideals are more beautiful than reality. Ultimately, they must believe that the source of the beauty and ugliness of ideals and reality lies primarily in the so-called human nature of liking the new and being curious. Why do people pursue ideals and are dissatisfied with reality? It is due to human nature's inherent liking for the new and being curious, not because ideals and reality themselves have anything truly desirable or unsatisfactory. Once an ideal becomes reality, even something beautiful becomes ugly. In this way, naturally, as long as we reform the human nature of liking the new and being curious, we will no longer pursue ideals and be dissatisfied with reality. Without worries or hardships, it is truly a good law for settling down and living one's life. Isn't running in and out just making trouble?

However, reality is, after all, very real, and it will never transform ugliness into beauty simply by reforming human nature. To transform ugliness into beauty, what is needed is precisely reform of reality by people. When reality itself has not been reformed to be as beautiful as the ideal, even if we reform human nature to a state of perfect goodness, we cannot make it as beautiful as the ideal. Moreover, this "even if" assumption is fundamentally impossible. To be honest, only when reality has been reformed to match the ideal will reality no longer be ugly, and only then can the so-called reform of human nature be truly spoken of. Currently, before human history has developed to the ideal stage, the separation between reality and ideals is an undeniable fact, but this separation is not created by so-called human nature; it exists in themselves. To eliminate this separation, there are many reformers who truly pursue ideals. Reformers pursue ideals precisely because they are dissatisfied with reality. Here, the words should be reversed: they are dissatisfied with reality and pursue ideals because reality and ideals themselves truly have things that are unsatisfactory and worth pursuing, not because reality and ideals are so-called reality and ideals. Once an ideal becomes reality, they will not be dissatisfied either. They only run in, never escape, and that is completely unrelated to their human nature.

So, why do some people often run in and out between ideals and reality? This is naturally because they have not recognized true ideals and reality, but merely arbitrarily constructed a phantom image in their minds. True ideals and reality are independent of people's minds. Only by objectively recognizing them can people avoid being confused and running in and out between a phantom image. However, this is mainly determined by the position of some people in society and history. Decaying feudal aristocrats will yearn for the luxury of the past and be dissatisfied with reality; the rising working masses are dissatisfied with reality and look forward to the beautiful future. Only our gentlemen and ladies, having neither the luxury of the past to yearn for nor the beautiful future to look forward to, cannot help but cling to reality. However, the incomplete and decadent reality will also make them feel dissatisfied. What to do? Only by pursuing an ideal that is a phantom image arbitrarily constructed in their minds. Illusions are always easy to shatter, and the result of pursuit is naturally disillusionment. When disillusionment occurs, they want to escape from reality, but when they cannot escape, they want to run into another ideal, and thus constantly run in and out between so-called ideals and reality. If we were to use a journey to visit scenic spots as an example, the difference should be said to be due to the lingering idea of yearning for the luxury of the past. And the general "leftover youths" of the old dynasty often love to express "ancient nostalgic feelings," which probably comes from here.

Let's still use the example of marriage, this besieged city: why do those on the outside want to rush in and take a look, while those inside want to escape? That is because those on the outside want to rush in to gain something, while those inside want to escape to avoid panic and danger. Once this besieged city becomes a free and open paradise, I think no one will want to escape anymore.

Baotu Spring 236

— Liu Ming

Before arriving in Jinan, I was enticed by the words in the Travel Notes of Lao Can: "Every household has spring water, and every household has weeping willows. Compared to the scenery of Jiangnan, it feels even more interesting." Therefore, having arrived in Jinan, I had to put my desire for sightseeing and curiosity on some famous springs first.

The first day, I went to see Baotu Spring. According to Travel Notes of Lao Can, "Baotu Spring is the number one spring among the seventy-two springs of Jinan Prefecture." And in the algae-covered spring, there is a weathered gray stone stele that marks the words "number one spring."

Upon entering, there are stalls selling various goods. Kui said that this is a bit like the Penglai Market in Shanghai. When leaning on the iron railing on the stone bridge to look at the spring water, the yellow-tiled Temple of Lu Zu, the teahouse singing drums, and the stalls selling small trinkets and fortune tellers gave people the feeling of the City God Temple in Shanghai.

There are about five or six streams of spring water, each with a diameter of about one foot wide. Like water columns, they rise from the mossy and algae-covered pond, carrying silvery white water flowers, protruding about two feet above the water surface. The sound roars vividly, covering up all the surrounding noise. The mood of the tourists also seems to shift from the city to the mountains all at once. There are two or three other streams that do not bubble out but surge like boiling water in a kettle. In the remaining areas, white bubbles often rise from the algae and moss. The saying that Jinan has spring water everywhere can probably be inferred from this.

Workers were digging in front of the pond, reportedly starting construction to install water pipes, with Baotu Spring as the base of the water source. The Temple of Lu Zu had a sign of the technical team of the tap water preparation committee hanging on it, and the police stood in front of the door, forbidding tourists from entering. It is thought that in the near future, this number one spring will benefit the residents of Jinan, but I don't know if travelers from afar will still have the opportunity to see it then?

The teahouse by the pond has a sign that says "singing drums." Peeking through the soft, thick cloth curtain, one sees comfortable rattan chairs and small tea tables covered with white cloth. There are not many patrons, mostly people of middle age or older. At that time, the drum had not yet started. In addition to sitting blankly, the guests were holding an old novel of some sort, pressing their necks down. The noise drowned out everything. One feels the long, leisurely air of the Eastern people unpleasantly hitting their brows. Kui said, "Walk away quickly, people will drag you in." I don't know why, but I also felt that this was not a good place to go. It was as if once you went in, a person's ambition and vigor would completely disappear.

At a stall selling antiques, I saw a Westerner examining them carefully, staying there for a long time. Could it be that, as Yosuke Tsurumi said in his article "The Charm of Beijing," "the calmness and slow pace of the Chinese" have "conquered the impatience of foreigners"? But I think those who have caught the "Eastern disease" can only be attributed to foreigners who "eat seventy-three eggs every day" or "eat a pound of cream every day." As for the Russian bums who drive buses in Shanghai or carry blankets and walk through the alleys, they are not seen to "think that China is unbearably good," are they?

If there were no spring water like water columns gushing out in a white surge, with a sound like mountain stream water, I feel that the surrounding environment would completely give people a sense of decline.

I Strove to Struggle Up Firmly 237

— Ding

The sun seemed like a ball of flames, emitting its brilliant golden light.

When I opened my eyes that were burning like fire, it had already shot into my eye sockets, causing a stinging sensation.

—Yes, I should get up.

I said quietly to myself.

However, after struggling for a while, I was still lying there. Indeed, I was terribly exhausted. My stomach was like a hungry stink bug, empty and sunken. My limbs were so weak and paralyzed.

Lying on a bed covered with rust, I deeply buried my thin body in the dirty and tattered quilt.

Silently looking up at the spider on the ceiling. It was active and busy.

Compared to it, I felt myself to be cowardly, incompetent, a useless waste. I did not strive for life, working hard like that tiny spider.

My heart had been deeply pierced by pain. Due to shame, due to wounds, my whole life was filled with confusion.

—Yes, I should get up.

—Yes, I must struggle to get up.

—Could I just keep lying there?

I asked myself and answered myself.

So, I made a decision: "Damn it, I have to struggle to get up!"

Gathering courage, using all my strength, I began to struggle desperately.

I felt a surge of heat, as if an electric current was running through my entire body, feeling hot all over. My face was like the skin of a roast duck.

However, I still couldn't get up. Disappointed and saddened, I quietly lay down again.

Unbearable, humiliating, terrifying, hungry, destroyed, I cursed my own life.

Recalling the words the landlord yelled at me and the indifferent attitude of my friends, I couldn't help but shiver. This was a cruel blow to me, shattering my soul to pieces.

Conscious of the coming of that terrible thing, I lay there stunned, as if there was nothing to hope for but death. So, I sighed deeply. Was there no hope for everything?

—It's over!—I shouted with all my life's strength.

—Isn't it? I have already run to the end of the world. Before me is a desolate scene with countless tombs. Isn't this the final resting place of mankind?

Thinking about it: my nerves went crazy. Could I just step onto the "road to destruction" like this?

—No! No!—I said: I still have hope, I still have strength, I still have life, I cannot die.

I have not paid a satisfactory price for life, I have not fulfilled my responsibilities. Can I just end my life like this?

I often want to use my youthful energy to ignite the life of mankind, to create the meaning of life, to praise the light. Isn't this my heavenly duty to life?

However, my efforts have made me feel discouraged, annoyed, and resentful. Have I really become desperate?

Indeed, in an environment of prejudice and adversity, I don't know how many promising young lives have been submerged.

My footprints have traveled all over the earth: desolate, dilapidated, filled with endless tragedies.

Everywhere there is:

"Closed for Business"

"Business for Sale"

"No Entry for Unauthorized Personnel"

Looking at those words, I felt heartbroken, disappointed, and indignant.

I am sick, I have no work, no life, no place where I can use my talents.

Thinking of this, I couldn't help but tremble again. Could I only helplessly watch myself perish?

—No! No! I should struggle to get up.—I answered myself.

So, I mustered my courage again and struggled! After groaning for a while, I lay down again, quietly and sadly.

Yes, I am very ill, no food, no clothes, no money to see a doctor or buy medicine. Let the devil take my life!

Then, a terrifying shadow of death suddenly appeared before my eyes. In the haze, I saw its cruel face, stretching out its long, bloody tongue, moving it in and out. It gradually approached my bed, opened its shining eyes, opened its giant mouth, and stretched its hairy hand to my neck.

—Ah!—I shouted loudly—I will not die! I cannot die! I don't want to die! I don't want to die! Extinguish this devil, drive out this devil. I want to live, defeat death!

My voice was filled with terror, filled with power. A flame of life rekindled in my heart. So, I firmly, suddenly, struggled to get up.

My heart was filled with an indescribable joy, so I smiled slightly. This was a victorious smile, how precious a smile. I haven't smiled in a long time. Long immersed in a life of suffering, had I not lost all joy in life?

At this moment, I stood healthy, invigorated, and proudly, and I emitted an unprecedented hope for everything.

Yes, I am still young, I have abundant youthful vitality, I have uncontrollable passion, I have blood and violence. Relying on this blood and strength, won't we be able to create earth-shattering miracles?

Winter Warmth 238

— TK

The Fly (3) 239

— Translated by Xi Dicen, based on Pirandello

The doctor turned around to look at him, as if wanting to devour him with his eyes.

"Sir, today is Sunday," Neli defended himself, smiling awkwardly. "I'm engaged!"

"Oh, you're engaged?" the doctor roared rebelliously. "Then hold this!"

While saying this, he stuffed the sick child into Neli's arms; then he grabbed each of the other little ones surrounding him, angrily bumping them against his legs.

"And this one! And this one! And this one! And this one! Beasts! Beasts!"

He turned his back to him, wanting to walk away, but then turned back, took back the sick little girl, and shouted to the two men:

"Go! Get the mules! I'm leaving right away."

Neli smiled, turned around, and walked down the stone steps after his brother. He was twenty years old; his fiancée, Rusa, sixteen: a rose! Seven children! Too few! He wanted twelve. He would feed them all with just the talent of a pair of good arms, always happy. Working, singing, using the strength of his skill to dig and sing. He was called the poet Liola for a reason. Then he felt that he was loved by everyone, loved for his attentive gentleness, his consistently good nature, and he even smiled at the air he was breathing. The sun had not yet tanned his skin, nor withered the deep golden color of his curly hair that so many women envied; if he quietly looked at a woman with his clear and bright eyes, then so many women's faces would blush, and their hearts would flutter.

The reason for his anxiety that day was not because of his cousin Chiaru, but because his Rusa had expressed her coyness to him, Rusa had been longing for that Sunday for seven days to be able to be intimate with him for a while. But could his conscience allow him to ignore this good deed of emergency aid? Poor Chiaru! He was engaged! How sad, suddenly, just like this! He was hitting almonds in the lower dam of Montelusa, the land of Ropa. Yesterday, Saturday morning, the sky looked like it was going to rain; but it didn't seem like there would be an immediate danger of showers.

But, around noon, Ropa said, "God does things at the right time, my children, I don't want to leave my almonds on the ground if it rains." As he said this, he ordered the female workers who had picked up the almonds to send them to the storage room to be shelled. "You," he said to the male workers who were hitting (Neli and Salo were also down there) "you can go there with the women and shell them if you want." "Okay," Chiaru said, "but do I still get a full shilling for the day?" "No," Ropa said, "I'll pay you half wages; the rest will be half wages, the same as the women workers." In fact, this was deceiving people! Why was there a reason to tell the male workers to stop working and not earn a full day's wages? The sky didn't rain, in fact, it didn't rain all day, nor did it rain that night. "'Half wages like the women workers'?" Chiaru asked. "I'm a man, you give me twenty-five pence a day for half wages, and I'll leave."

But he didn't leave: he stayed there until the evening, waiting for his two cousins, who were willing to shell with the female workers, to get half the money. However, tired of standing and watching for a while, he went to a nearby stable, lay down and fell asleep, and told someone to wake him up when it was time to go home.
